401 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Ritchmount Partnership v. Board of Supervisors of Elections


Nos. 161, 162, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


283 Md. 48; 388 A.2d 523; 1978 Md. LEXIS 406



June 26, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Childs, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decrees of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged separate judgments of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which upheld the constitutionality of Charter of Anne Arundel County, Md., art. III, § 308, which conferred upon the people of a home rule county the power of referendum over local legislative enactments where it was neither delegated by the General Assembly nor expressly reserved to the inhabitants of charter counties by the Constitution.


OVERVIEW: In ratifying § 308, the voters retained the right to approve or reject by way of petition and popular election ordinances of the county council. The county council enacted new zoning legislation. Instead of challenging the new ordinance through litigation, opponents of the zoning action appealed to the voters through referendum. Appellees, the Board of Supervisors of Elections of Anne Arundel County (board), ordered the question placed on the ballot. The voters rejected the legislation. The landowners claimed that the board lacked authority to approve the citizen referendum petitions and instituted suits in the circuit court that challenged the validity of § 308 and the zoning referendum. The circuit court issued a declaratory decree that upheld the referendum article and election. The court granted certiorari and affirmed. The adoption of a home rule charter that included the referendum process was an exercise of the right to make provision for any form of government the people deemed suitable for their needs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decrees of the circuit court that upheld the referendum process that struck down zoning legislation and determined that the previous zoning legislation was revived by the voters' referendum vote.

 

402 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Folly Farms I, Inc. v. Trustees of Clients' Sec. Trust Fund of The Bar


Misc. No. 10, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


282 Md. 659; 387 A.2d 248; 1978 Md. LEXIS 397



June 5, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Claimants' exceptions to final determination by Trustees of the Clients' Security Trust Fund of the Bar of Maryland.



DISPOSITION: Exceptions sustained; costs to be paid by the Trustees of the Clients' Security Trust Fund of the Bar of Maryland.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff clients appealed the decision of defendant trustees of a bar association trust fund, which denied clients' claims after the court had vacated its earlier decision and remanded the claim.


OVERVIEW: A voluntary fund was established by a city bar association to maintain the integrity of the legal profession by reasonably reimbursing losses caused by defalcations of members of the bar of the State of Maryland, acting either as attorneys or as fiduciaries. Clients filed a claim with the trustees seeking reimbursement of losses caused by the defalcations of their attorney. The claim was denied on the ground that the proximate cause of the defalcations stemmed from their attorney's having been made a corporate officer with the authorization to sign checks on its behalf. Clients appealed to the court, which remanded the matter to the trustees. The trustees denied the claims again and the clients appealed. The court reversed, holding that the trustees were to pay the claim. The court held that the trustees had been too strict in their determination of what constituted an attorney-client relationship. In determining whether such a relationship existed, the court applied the "but for" standard: but for the fact that the dishonest attorney enjoyed an attorney-client relationship with the claimant at the time of or prior to the loss, the loss would not have occurred.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the clients' exceptions and awarded them costs.

 

403 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


White v. Prince George's County


No. 67, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


282 Md. 641; 387 A.2d 260; 1978 Md. LEXIS 396



June 5, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cross appeals from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowie and Blackwell, JJ., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Costs to be equally divided.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers brought an action against defendant county for a refund of an alleged recording tax overpayment, and to reduce to judgment an order of refund by the tax court. The Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) granted the taxpayers summary judgment as to the tax court order, but granted the county's demurrer on the refund claim. Both parties appealed, and the court granted the county's petition for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: In a prior action, the tax court held that the county's recordation rate exceeded that allowed by statute, and the taxpayers were entitled to a refund. The court affirmed that decision. In response to that case, chapter 129 of the Acts of 1976 was enacted, ratifying the county's rate retroactively except as to any actions which were res judicata. In the present action, the taxpayers argued that because the facts and issues of a second refund claim were identical to the prior action, except for the instrument recorded, and because the county refused to make payment from the prior action, they were not required to exhaust their administrative remedies. Noting that there was no common law action for recovery of taxes voluntarily paid as a mistake of law, the court held that the taxpayers' proper remedy was through the statutory procedure set out in Md. Code art. 81, §§ 215-217. The court rejected the county's claim that the prior action was a nullity because the appeal from the tax court's order was based on a statute since held unconstitutional. In any event, the tax court's decision was a final order, making the action res judicata for purposes of chapter 129 of the Acts of 1976.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court which granted summary judgment to the taxpayers on the action to reduce the tax court order to judgment and sustained the county's demurrer on the taxpayers' claim for a second refund.

 

404 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Montgomery County v. Fields Road Corp.


No. 109, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


282 Md. 575; 386 A.2d 344; 1978 Md. LEXIS 391



May 23, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Latham, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County reversed, and case remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) that sustained appellee landlord's demurrer to the county's bill of complaint. The county brought this action to enjoin the landlord from violating regulations that required landlords to report on minority tenants and applicants. The trial court held that the regulations violated the United States Constitution and the Maryland Declaration of Rights.


OVERVIEW: The regulations required landlords with 25 or more rental units to report on the number of minority tenants and applicants. The circuit court held that the distinction between owners of 25 or more units and owners of a lesser number of units was arbitrary and violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. On appeal, the court reversed. The court noted the testimony of a county witness that over 90 percent of the complaints concerning housing discrimination related to apartments rather than houses and that the regulations covered a very high percentage of the units in the county. According to the court, this testimony demonstrated a reasonable basis for the distinction drawn. The trial court also found that one of the goals of the regulations was to make landlords cognizant of the percentage of minorities in their units and that such an objective was not justified absent a finding of past discrimination. The county argued that if landlords were aware of the racial makeup of their units, they would examine their practices and eliminate unconscious or unknowing discrimination. The court agreed with the county that its goal was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that sustained the landlord's demurrer to the county's bill of complaint.

 

405 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Edgewood Nursing Home v. Maxwell


No. 144, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


282 Md. 422; 384 A.2d 748; 1978 Md. LEXIS 376



April 24, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Greenfeld, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employer and insurer, challenged a judgment by the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland) that granted a workmen's compensation claim for dependency benefits filed on behalf of appellee decedent's daughter under § 67(6) of the Workmen's Compensation Act, Md. Ann. Code art. 101 (1957, 164 Repl. Vol., 1975 Cum. Supp.).


OVERVIEW: After dependency benefits were awarded to the decedent's daughter, appellants argued that the lower court's interpretation of § 67(6) deprived them of due process of law. Appellants argued that the interpretation of § 67(6) permitting recovery in the absence of a casual connection between the death and the employment other than a mere occurrence in the course of employment was repugnant to the Fourteenth Amendment because it made the employer an involuntary insurer of the life and health of his employees under circumstances where such liability did not rest upon the employer-employee relationship. The court affirmed the award of benefits to the decedent's daughter because the employer's obligation under § 67(6) to pay compensation on behalf of an employee injured in the course of his employment by the wilful or negligent act of a third party did rest upon the employer-employee relationship. The court found that the injury in a sense was work-related even though it arose for personal reasons not attributable to the work environment. The court concluded that it occurred within the course of employment on the employer's premises at a time when the decedent was obliged to be at work.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that granted workmen's compensation claim for dependency benefits filed on behalf of the decedent's daughter.

 

406 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 70, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


282 Md. 314; 384 A.2d 709; 1978 Md. LEXIS 368



April 6, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Carroll County, Weant, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; remanded to that court with instructions to reverse the judgment of the Circuit Court for Carroll County and to remand for a new trial. Costs to be paid by Anne Arundel County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of certiorari from a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed defendant's convictions for armed robbery, assault with intent to murder, larceny, conspiracy and unlawful use of a handgun in connection with two holdups.


OVERVIEW: The court granted certiorari to determine whether voluntary incriminatory statements, given after a valid waiver of Miranda rights, were nevertheless inadmissible against defendant, when such statements were obtained by police following an unnecessary delay in producing the accused before a judicial officer in violation of former Md. Code Ann. § 709a. Prompt presentment after arrest assured impartial judicial supervision of defendant's rights at the earliest stage of detention. The court held that the prompt presentment requirement was mandatory and was therefore binding on the police. Further, any statement, voluntary or otherwise, obtained from an arrestee during a period of unnecessary delay in producing him before a judicial officer, was subject to exclusion when offered into evidence against defendant. Moreover, unless defendant waived his right to prompt presentment before a judicial officer, both statements implicating him in the crimes should have been excluded from evidence, having been obtained in clear violation of Md. Code Ann. § 723a.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals and remanded to that court with instructions to reverse the judgment of the trial court and remand for a new trial.

 

407 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Attorney Gen. v. Johnson


No. 108, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


282 Md. 274; 385 A.2d 57; 1978 Md. LEXIS 367



April 5, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed April 21, 1978; Denied April 21, 1978. Appeal to the Supreme Court of the United States Filed May 1, 1978.
Appeal dismissed by Johnson v. Attorney Gen. of Maryland, 439 U.S. 805, 58 L. Ed. 2d 97, 99 S. Ct. 60, 1978 U.S. LEXIS 2483 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two appeals in one record from the Baltimore City Court; Greenfeld, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded to the Baltimore City Court with directions to enter a judgment declaring that Chapter 235 of the Laws of 1976, codified as Md. Code (1974, 1977 Cum. Supp.), §§ 3-2A01 to 3-2A09 of the Courts Article, is constitutional. Costs to be paid by the appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state officials sought review of a judgment of the Baltimore City Court (Maryland) that held the Health Care Malpractice Claims Act, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 3-2A01to 3-2A09 (1974 & 1977 Cum. Supp.) was unconstitutional because it vested judicial power in an administrative agency and imposed procedural and monetary impediments that denied reasonable access to the courts and the right to trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellee claimants wished to sue a hospital for medical malpractice. Prior to the time their claim arose, the Health Care Malpractice Claims Act (Act), Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 3-2A01to 3-2A09 (1974 & 1977 Cum. Supp.), was passed, which required the submission of certain malpractice claims to an arbitration panel for initial ascertainment of liability and damages before the matter could be submitted to a court of law for final determination. Appellees filed suit claiming the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court agreed, finding that the Act impermissibly vested judicial power in an administrative agency and imposed procedural and monetary impediments that denied reasonable access to the courts and the right to trial by jury. Appellant state officials sought review, and the court reversed and remanded. The essence of judicial power was the final authority to render and enforce a judgment. This was not a power vested with the arbitration panel. The right to jury trial was not violated because any contested issues were permitted to ultimately go before a jury. The court further found that the Act did not violate the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: Judgment finding that the Health Care Malpractice Claims Act (Act) was unconstitutional was reversed and remanded. The Act did not impermissibly vest the arbitration panel with judicial function because the panel did not have final authority to render and enforce a judgment. Further, the right to jury trial was not infringed because any contested issues of fact could ultimately be submitted to a jury.

 

408 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Zellinger v. CRC Dev. Corp.


No. 65, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 614; 380 A.2d 1064; 1977 Md. LEXIS 619



December 22, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed January 23, 1978; Denied January 31, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two appeals from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City and Baltimore City Court; Greenfeld, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Baltimore City Court and Circuit Court of Baltimore City affirmed; appellants to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the judgments from the Circuit Court of Baltimore and the Baltimore City Court (Maryland), which upheld Baltimore City, Md., Ordinance 137 (1976) and denied injunctive relief restraining appellees, owners and developers, from proceeding with the construction of the housing project authorized under Ordinance 137. Appellees, mayor, city council, owners, and developers, filed a petition for certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed an action in the city court challenging the validity of Ordinance 137, which authorized the construction and operation of a housing complex for the elderly. At the same time, they filed an action in the circuit court to enjoin appellees from proceeding with the construction. The lower courts upheld the ordinance and denied injunctive relief. The property owners appealed, but prior to consideration by the appellate court, appellees' petition for certiorari was granted. The court affirmed the lower courts' judgments. The property owners did not show that the city abused its discretion, under Baltimore City, Md., Code art. 30, § § 4.5-1d and 4.0-2c, by acting inconsistently or unfairly in granting or denying other conditional use applications. Thus, the mere retention of the power to pass on conditional uses did not violate the uniformity mandate of Md. Ann. Code art. 66B, § 2.02. Likewise, the evidence was insufficient to overcome the presumption that Baltimore City, Md., Code art. 30, § § 4.5-1d and 4.0-2c were constitutional. The Zoning Board's approval was not a condition precedent to the right and power of city council to approve the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellees' petition for certiorari and affirmed the lower court's judgments, which upheld the challenged ordinance and denied the injunctive relief requested by the property owners to enjoin appellees from proceeding with the construction of the housing project authorized under the ordinance.

Wheeler v. State


No. 66, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 593; 380 A.2d 1052; 1977 Md. LEXIS 618; 3 Media L. Rep. 1607



December 12, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed January 11, 1978; Denied January 20, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Liss, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; case remanded to that court for remand to the Criminal Court of Baltimore with direction to dismiss the indictment; costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the decision of the trial court convicting defendant of distributing an obscene magazine in violation of section 418 of the Obscene Matter Act (Act), Md. Code art. 27 (1957, 1976 Repl. Vol.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a salesman at a local adult bookstore, was convicted of distributing an obscene magazine in violation of § 418 of the Act. Section 417(2) of that Act defined excluded from the definition of the word "person" those operating a theatre that showed motion pictures. The appellate court affirmed the conviction and the court granted a petition for a writ of certiorari. The court reversed the conviction and held that § 418 of the Act, considered with § 417(2), was unconstitutional on its fact in that it denied him equal protection of the laws. The court did not think that the mere possibility of further distribution after a sale in a bookstore, in itself, warranted the classification. The bookstore employee, or any other person not within the exempted class, who distributed that same program, would have been subject to punishment for violation of the statute. Thus, the law operated on some persons and not upon others like situated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for distributing an obscene magazine and ordered the appellate court to remand to the trial court with direction to dismiss the indictment.

 

410 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. State


No. 53, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 538; 380 A.2d 49; 1977 Md. LEXIS 614; 98 A.L.R.3d 1275



December 8, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed December 20, 1977; Denied January 3, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Arabian, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; case remanded to that court with directions that it remand the case to the Criminal Court of Baltimore for a new trial; costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Court of Special Appeals, Criminal Court of Baltimore (Maryland) of rape, perverted sexual practice, and larceny.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had asked his wife to go to his apartment to get a ring which he had stolen from the victim. He contended on appeal that this evidence was a privileged confidential communication between him and his wife, and was improperly admitted in evidence in violation of Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 9-105 (1974). The court found that the evidence did not suggest that his wife disclosed his communication to a third party, nor did the circumstances require disclosure. In addition, the nature of the communication indicated that it was intended to remain confidential. The court found that the communication was confidential and consequently protected by the statute from disclosure, and that the fact that defendant and his wife were separated at the time of the communication, or that their marriage had little to commend it, did not bar application of the privilege. Nor did the fact that defendant had already been served with divorce papers at the time he claimed the privilege bar its application. Further the court found that the lower court was wrong in concluding that the privilege was not applicable where the confidential communication was made in furtherance of a crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to determine whether the erroneous admission of the privileged communication between defendant and his wife amounted to harmless error.

Aviles v. Eshelman Electric Corp.


No. 33, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 529; 379 A.2d 1227; 1977 Md. LEXIS 613



December 8, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed January 6, 1978; Denied January 20, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowie, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County reversed and case remanded to that court with instructions to dismiss the consolidated cases. Costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which allowed appellee subcontractors to foreclose their liens on the property owners' land.


OVERVIEW: The property owners executed a contract with the general contractor for the construction of a dwelling on the property owners' land. To assist them in financing, the property owners' mother arranged for a series of loans. The general contractor experienced financial difficulties and eventually resulted in bankruptcy, which caused abandonment of construction altogether. The subcontractors gave notice to the property owners of their intention to file liens against the property. The subcontractors filed the liens, but the property owners argued that they failed to comply with the statutory provisions. The court agreed and reversed the lower court's decision. The record disclosed that not one of the subcontractors complied with all of the statutory provisions. In addition, they failed to timely file their liens, which clearly barred their actions. Therefore, there was no basis to enforce any of the liens and claims of the subcontractors.


OUTCOME: The judgment allowing the subcontractors to foreclose their liens against the property owners was reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss the cases.

 

412 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Maryland Classified Employees Asso. v. Anderson


No. 20, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 496; 380 A.2d 1032; 1977 Md. LEXIS 610



December 7, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Harford County; Higinbothom, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county employees and employee association, filed a petition for a writ of mandamus and for damages against appellees, employer and county officials, by which they sought to enforce an arbitration award regarding a wage increase pursuant to Harford County, Md., Code § 201B(h)(5) (1965). The Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland) denied the petition.


OVERVIEW: Under the binding arbitration provision of Harford County, Md., Code § 201B(h)(5) (1965), the county employer was to implement an arbitrator's award of a wage increase for its employees. The county did not implement the award and the employee association, on behalf of the employees, filed a petition for a writ of mandamus and for damages against the employer and other county officials. The employer raised the defense that the binding arbitration provision was invalid. The trial court issued an interlocutory order in which it denied the employees' motion to prohibit the employer from raising the defense of the invalidity of its own municipal ordinance. The trial court then denied the employees' petition. In affirming the trial court, the court first held that the motion to prohibit was properly denied because the employer could challenge the validity of the ordinance where the duties involved were ministerial. Second, the court held that the ordinance was invalid because it attempted to bind the employer in the exercise of legislative discretion over the compensation of its public employees, which was not authorized by either a public general law or by the county charter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied the petition of the county employees and the employee association for writ of mandamus and damages against the employer and county officials.

 

413 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Baltimore v. Kelso Corp.


No. 42, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 514; 380 A.2d 216; 1977 Md. LEXIS 611



December 7, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas of Baltimore City; Cardin, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Baltimore City dated October 29, 1976, vacated and case remanded to that court for further proceedings to determine the amount of compensation to be paid by Baltimore City for the land taken. Costs to be paid by the appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city filed eight separate condemnation petitions against parcels of land owned by appellee property owner. The property owner filed a motion to dismiss the city's quick-take petitions and thus divest it of title and possession of the property. The Court of Common Pleas of Baltimore City (Maryland) entered an order granting its motion to divest the city of possession and title to the property. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner alleged that it was not necessary for the city to take the land and that the city had fraudulently used its zoning powers in order to deprive it of just compensation by adversely affecting the value of the real estate. On appeal, the court held that Baltimore, Md., Code of Pub. Loc. Laws § 21-16(a), (c) (1969, 1977 Cum. Supp.) made clear that, unless the right or power to condemn title was challenged, if the city had complied with the procedural requirements of § 21-16 a property owner had no basis for attacking the immediate taking of his property under the statute. Because the property owner had never contended that the city did not comply with the formal requirements mandated by § 21-16(a), and had repeatedly emphasized that it did not dispute the city's right and power to condemn, title and possession vested in the city 10 days after the property owner withdrew its original answer and objection to the quick-take petitions, and could not presently be attacked. Thus, the property owner's motion to strike the trial court's orders granting immediate title and possession to the city was inappropriate and the trial court erred in granting it.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order and remanded the case for further proceedings to determine the amount of compensation to be paid by the city for the land taken.

 

414 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State Dep't of Assessments & Taxation v. Clark


No. 23, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 385; 380 A.2d 28; 1977 Md. LEXIS 601



November 4, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Fairbanks, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; case remanded for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion; costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state tax department sought review of a decision from the County Court of Special Appeals, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The sewer district imposed a moratorium on new lines, and the taxpayers sought a reassessment of their property under Md. Code Ann., Revenue and Taxes § 67. The tax department superintendent recommended a twenty-five percent reduction, which was approved by the tax court. The taxpayers filed a separate declaratory action in the county trial court and sought to enjoin collection of the property taxes until they received a rehearing. The trial court granted their motion for summary judgment, and the tax department sought review. It argued that the county trial court lacked jurisdiction to review § 67 proceedings. The court found that the county trial court did not ordinarily have inherent power to review § 67 proceedings because the legislature had expressly provided for a method of administrative review. It found that the trial court did have jurisdiction to determine if § 67, as applied to the taxpayers, was constitutional. Because the trial court did have jurisdiction over constitutionality as applied, it should have granted summary judgment in favor of the tax department because the taxpayers failed to show a genuine dispute as to any material fact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions for the trial court to enter judgment in favor of the tax department.

 

415 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Police Comm'r of Baltimore City v. Dowling


No. 41, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 412; 379 A.2d 1007; 1977 Md. LEXIS 602



November 4, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Greenfeld, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed; appellee to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police commissioner sought review of an order of the Baltimore City Court (Maryland), which ruled that the police commissioner could not increase the penalty imposed by the Police Department Trial Board in favor of appellee police officer.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was investigated for misconduct. The Police Department Trial Board recommended that he serve 80 hours of duty without pay. The police commissioner then directed that the officer be terminated. The officer appealed to city court, and that court reinstated the original penalty. On appeal, the court reversed the reinstatement of the decision of the trial board. The court held that Law-Enforcement Officers Bill of Rights, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 727-734A did not prevent the police commissioner from dismissing an officer notwithstanding a recommendation for a lesser punishment by a hearing board. The court ruled that the fact that Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 732 referred to decisions rendered in accordance with Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 730-731 did not compel a finding of inconsistency between the Law-Enforcement Officers Bill of Rights and Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 732. The court reasoned that the hearing board would meet and hold hearings, that it would make its findings under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 731, and that those findings would be transmitted to the police commissioner for his ultimate decision. An appeal would lie from the police commissioner's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, which found that the police commissioner could not increase a penalty imposed by the Police Department Trial Board.

 

416 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Weaver v. Prince George's County


No. 2, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 349; 379 A.2d 399; 1977 Md. LEXIS 598



November 3, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Bowling, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellants to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, tenants and landlords, appealed the decision of the Maryland Court of Special Appeals, which reversed the chancellor's ruling that the application of Prince George's County Multifamily Occupancy Tax to persons receiving military housing allowances exceeded defendant county's authority in plaintiffs' action for a declaration judgment.


OVERVIEW: The tenants and landlords contested the constitutionality of the occupancy tax under the uniform taxation mandate of Article 15 of the Declaration of Rights. The keystone of the challenge to the occupancy tax was whether the tax was a direct tax on the tenant's property or whether it was an indirect excise tax on the privilege of using or occupying a rented multifamily residential unit. The court examined the designation placed upon the tax by the Legislature, the subject matter of the tax, and the incidents of the tax, as in the manner in which it was assessed and the measure of the tax, and affirmed the decision. At no point in the state act or the county ordinance was there any indication that the tax was intended as a direct charge on a tenant's possessory estate. Thus, the tax appeared to be a levy on the use and occupancy of a dwelling rather than an assessment directly against any property interest in the tenant's hands. The court held that the occupancy tax was an excise tax imposed or laid with a political view for the good government and benefit of the community, and was therefore not subject to the uniformity requirements of Article 15 of the Declaration of Rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

 

417 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Montgomery County v. Woodward & Lothrop, Inc.


No. 104, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 686; 376 A.2d 483; 1977 Md. LEXIS 877



July 15, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Miller, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County reversing Resolution 7-1849 of the Montgomery County Council vacated; case remanded for the entry of an order in conformity with this opinion; costs to be paid by the parties identified in the opinion as the appellee property owners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: These appeals drew into question the validity of a rezoning by sectional map amendment. Plaintiffs, ten aggrieved property owners whose properties had been "downzoned" by the amendment, appealed to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland). The circuit court reversed the trial court's resolution granting the sectional map amendment. Defendant county and others appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with the trial court that the geographic requirement for comprehensive rezoning had been satisfied. All other requisite indicia of comprehensiveness were also present. Underlying adoption of the sectional map amendment was a well thought out, carefully considered and extensively studied plan, correlated to the common needs of the area. There was massive participation in the planning process. The requirement for a comprehensive plan was met because due consideration was given to the common needs of a particular district. The aggrieved property owners had not overcome the presumption that the rezoning was valid and bore the necessary relationship to the general public interest and welfare. The circuit court erred in holding that even though the rezoning was comprehensive, precedent mandated that the aggrieved property owners be afforded a right to cross-examine witnesses at the sectional map amendment hearings before the county council.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the circuit court and remanded the case.

 

418 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Baltimore v. State


No. 52, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


281 Md. 217; 378 A.2d 1326; 1977 Md. LEXIS 590



July 15, 1977  
October 25, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Greenfeld, J., and two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Greenfeld, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city and intervenor citizens sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland) which granted summary judgment upholding defendant state's enactment of Ch. 671 of the Acts of 1977 for the acquisition and conversion of property for a correctional institution. The city and the citizens contended that the state was required to comply with the city's zoning ordinance and that the enactment was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature enacted Ch. 671 of the Acts of 1977, which provided for the state's acquisition and construction of property in the city for use as a correctional institution. The city brought an action against the state, claiming that the state was bound to comply with the city's zoning ordinance and that Ch. 671 violated Md. Const. art. III, § 29, Md. Const. art. III, § 52(8)(a), and Md. Const. art. III, § 15(1). The city and citizens also claimed that the state violated certain statutory requirements regarding the acquisition of property and compliance with the Maryland Environmental Policy Act. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment for the state, finding that the city had no authority to subject the state to its zoning ordinance where the state had not manifested an intent be bound by the provisions of the Zoning Enabling Act. The court also concluded that the enactment complied with constitutional requirements relating to its title, limitation to a single purpose, and enactment within the 90 day legislative session and that it was not necessary for the state to comply with certain statutory requirements regarding the project.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for the state, in an action by the city contending that the state was required to comply with the city's zoning ordinance and that the state's legislative enactment was unconstitutional.

 

419 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Bartram v. State


No. 148, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 616; 374 A.2d 1144; 1977 Md. LEXIS 872



July 7, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Baltimore County, MacDaniel, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought certiorari review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted her of second degree murder and a related handgun offense.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented by defendant in her petition for the writ of certiorari was: Did the state's conduct with regard to the grand juries that considered her case mandate that the 1974 indictment be dismissed? The court affirmed the judgments and answered the question in the negative. The court stated (1) that the grand jury was an accusatory body that heard only one side of the case, not a trier of fact that heard both sides of the case and it made its determination accordingly; (2) that the grand jury was an investigatory body that could return an indictment based not upon testimony before it, but on knowledge of its members gleaned in the community from which the grand jury panel was drawn; (3) that the competency of testimony before a grand jury would not be inquired into by the courts; and (4) that indictments could be returned based upon hearsay or illegally obtained evidence. The court concluded that there was no conduct on the part of the state or other imperfection in the grand jury proceedings which mandated the dismissal of the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of second degree murder and a related handgun offense. The defendant was also ordered to pay costs.

 

420 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


O. C. Taxpayers for Equal Rights, Inc. v. Ocean City


No. 111, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 585; 375 A.2d 541; 1977 Md. LEXIS 870



July 6, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed July 13, 1977; Denied July 13, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Worcester County; Simpkins, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Circuit Court for Worcester County vacated, and case remanded to that court for entry of judgment in accordance with this opinion. Petitioners to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, non-resident property owners, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland), which sustained a city ordinance adopted by defendants, the mayor and city council, changing the qualifications for voters in city elections while holding invalid an ordinance creating a classification between non-resident property owners registered before the ordinance's enactment and all other non-resident property owners.


OVERVIEW: The voting franchise originally extended not only to residents but also to non-residents owning real estate. The mayor and city council adopted a charter amendment resolution which changed the qualifications of voters by prohibiting non-resident property owners from voting. However, another resolution created a "grandfather clause" that allowed non-resident property owners on the voter rolls as of the date the resolutions to remain on the voter rolls. Several non-residents subsequently attempted to register to vote. When they were denied registration, they filed a declaratory action asserting that the resolutions were unconstitutional. The trial court held that the resolution changing the qualifications was proper, but found that the resolution creating the "grandfather clause" was unconstitutional as violative of Equal Protection. On appeal, the non-resident property owners asserted that the two provisions were not severable, making both invalid. The court held that resolutions were validly enacted, and that the legislative intent and history supported the finding of severability. The classification violated Equal Protection, making only the second resolution invalid.


OUTCOME: The court agreed with the trial court's order finding the second resolution invalid and severable from the first, but vacated the order and remanded the case because the trial court adjudicated additional matters that should not have been reached and did not deal with all of the resolutions challenged.

 

421 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Du Bois v. College Park


No. 135, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 525; 375 A.2d 1098; 1977 Md. LEXIS 866



July 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Mattingly, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded to the Circuit Court for Prince George's County for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. Appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to certiorari, plaintiff registered voters, individually and for those similarly situated, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which dismissed for lack of standing their action for a declaratory judgment that the councilmanic districts of defendant city were unconstitutionally apportioned.


OVERVIEW: The registered voters contended that their votes were debased and that they were deprived of equal protection of the laws in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment because of malapportionment. The city contended that the registered voters were not bona fide residents of the city and therefore lacked standing to maintain the action. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the action and remanded. The court found, inter alia, that the trial court erred in allowing the city to present evidence that the registered voters actually resided in areas other than the city and therefore should not have been allowed to register as voters. The city could not challenge the registered voter' status as qualified voters because a statutory remedy was available to challenge such qualifications. The statutory remedy was the exclusive method for challenging the qualifications of the registered voters. Also, it was of no consequence if a registered voter lived in a district, which was over-represented; the voter still had standing because residents of a legislative district, which received constitutional treatment under a redistricting plan, had standing to maintain an appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the registered voter's action for a declaratory judgment that the councilmanic districts of the city were unconstitutionally apportioned, and the court remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

422 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Rand v. Rand


No. 147, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 508; 374 A.2d 900; 1977 Md. LEXIS 864; 90 A.L.R.3d 150



June 30, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Miller, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals vacated; case remanded to that Court with directions that it remand the matter to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County for the entry of a decree in conformity with the views expressed in this opinion; costs to be paid by the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a trial court's decree that ordered appellee father to pay less than the total amount required for a child's support. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reduced the father's support obligation, holding that under Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 46 and Md. Code Ann. art. 72A, § 1 (1957) the mother was obligated to contribute to support, and the mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: When a trial court declined to order a father to pay the full amount that it determined was necessary for a child's support, the mother appealed contending that he was obligated to pay support up to the limit of his available income after proper expenses were paid. The court held that the parental duty to support a child was not primarily the father's obligation but was to be shared by the parents in accordance with their respective financial resources. The language of art. 72A, § 1 was sufficient to reject the common law rule that imposed a support duty only on the father. Although the courts had failed to interpret that statute to require both parents to share the duty of support, any remaining doubt was eliminated by the passage of the equal rights amendment, Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 46. In allocating the responsibility for child support, courts were not permitted to consider the sex of the parent as a factor because child support awards were required to be made on a sexless basis.


OUTCOME: The court agreed with the conclusion reached by the lower court, but vacated its judgment and remanded the matter so that the lower court could determine the parental support obligation of each party in accordance with the views expressed in the opinion.

 

423 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Ward v. State


No. 87, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 485; 374 A.2d 1118; 1977 Md. LEXIS 863; 89 A.L.R.3d 874



June 24, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowie, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) for operating an aircraft in a reckless manner in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 1A, § 10-1002. Defendant was convicted by the district court and was tried de novo by a judge in the circuit court. In a civil proceeding, the Federal Aviation Administration determined that defendant had violated seven federal aviation regulations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the holder of a valid student aircraft pilot license and medical certificate issued by the Federal Aviation Administration (FAA). After completing an instructional flight, defendant and his instructor enjoyed a dinner complete with pre- and postprandial liquid refreshment. The following morning, defendant decided to practice some "touch and gos" during the course of which, he "buzzed" nearby apartments. His activities were observed by a Maryland police officer in a helicopter who followed the plane back to the airport. Defendant was arrested and an examination showed that his blood alcohol level was 0.17 percent. On appeal, defendant argued that the state was precluded from prosecution because the statute proscribing his conduct was preempted by the Federal Aviation Act, 49 U.S.C.S. § 1301 et seq. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court found that it was the clear intent of congress that criminal prosecution of defendant's conduct be left with the states and that there was no conflict within the contemplation of the doctrine of preemption between the state and federal laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for operating an aircraft in a reckless manner and held that the statute challenged by defendant was not preempted by federal law.

State v. Schuller


No. 89, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 305; 372 A.2d 1076; 1977 Md. LEXIS 847



May 6, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Miller, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County affirmed. Costs to be paid by Montgomery County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed a petition for a writ of certiorari to review a decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which reversed the district court's conviction of defendants for unlawful picketing in violation of Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 580.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested and charged with unlawful picketing of a residential neighborhood after they refused to stop protesting government nuclear armament in front of the home of a government official. After a trial, defendants were found guilty. The circuit court dismissed the charges because it determined that Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 580A was unconstitutional. The state argued that the regulation was not violative of the First and Fourteenth Amendments because it was a valid exercise of the state's police power to protect individual privacy by enacting reasonable time, place, and manner regulations irrespective of content. The state also argued that the exemption of labor related picketing did not create a classification which violated the Equal Protection Clause, as the classification served a compelling state interest. The court affirmed the decision because the regulation was drawn too broadly and because it encompassed within its scope activity which was constitutionally safeguarded. The court also held that the residential picketing provision were not severable from the labor related picketing provisions which were exempted from criminal prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment and dismissed the charges against defendants for unlawful picketing of a residential neighborhood.

 

425 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Squire v. State


No. 113, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 132; 368 A.2d 1019; 1977 Md. LEXIS 834



April 15, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Dorf, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed and case remanded to that court with instructions to reverse the judgment of the Criminal Court of Baltimore and remand the case to that latter court for a new trial. Costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought certiorari review after the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed his conviction for assault with intent to murder and unlawful use of a handgun, despite an error in the jury instructions with respect to the burden of proof.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial, the trial court instructed the jury that defendant had the burden of proof with respect to the defense of self-defense. The appellate court affirmed. The court reversed. Although defendant had not objected to the instruction at trial, the court exercised its discretion to take notice of plain error. Defendant was tried only four days after the United States Supreme Court issued a decision that changed the law with respect to the burden of proving self-defense. The state had admitted that the jury instruction was prejudicially erroneous. The court concluded that defendant's failure to have objected had not resulted from trial tactics or inadvertence, but from counsel's belief that the instruction was in accord with Maryland and federal law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

Harford County v. Schultz


No. 139, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


280 Md. 77; 371 A.2d 428; 1977 Md. LEXIS 830



April 5, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Harford County; Higinbothom, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree vacated and case remanded for the passage of an order dismissing the bill; Harford County to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county petitioned for a writ of certiorari, seeking review of an order from the Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland), which declared two proposed amendments to its county charter to be valid bills that could be submitted to the county voters. Appellee Board of Supervisors of Elections for Harford County (board) had certified one of the bills, and the county had sought a declaratory judgment that both bills were invalid.


OVERVIEW: In 1976, the county council proposed two amendments to the county charter. One bill was vetoed by the county executive and passed over his veto, and the other bill allegedly was certified to the board prior to the expiration of time for consideration of the proposal by the county executive. The county filed a declaratory judgment action against the board, seeking a declaration that both bills were invalid and an injunction against advertising or placing these bills on the election ballot. The chancellor held both bills to be valid and proper legislative acts to be submitted to the county voters at the November 1976 election. The court granted certiorari and ordered that the lower court's decree be vacated and remanded for an order of dismissal, finding that the lower court lacked jurisdiction to hear the case because there was no justiciable issue. The court held that to come within the purview of the Declaratory Judgment Act, there had to be an actual controversy, and found that the county's rights, status, or other legal relations had not been adversely affected by its own deliberately intended enactment of amendments to its own charter.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decree declaring the bills valid and remanded the case for an order dismissing the county's action for declaratory judgment that the bills were invalid.

Donnelly Advertising Corp. v. Baltimore


No. 138, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 660; 370 A.2d 1127; 1977 Md. LEXIS 930; 7 ELR 20397



March 21, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Cole, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree vacated; case remanded for the entry of a decree in conformance with this opinion; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advertiser sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which found in favor of appellee city and held that a challenged billboard ordinance was valid and constitutional, in the declaratory judgment action brought by the advertiser.


OVERVIEW: As part of an urban renewal plan, the city enacted an ordinance that prohibited signs other than those identifying the property where they were installed or identifying the use conducted therein. It also mandated the removal of all billboards within the project area that were larger than 60 feet without compensation for their removal. The advertiser owned several billboards in the affected area and sought to have the ordinance declared invalid and unconstitutional. The trial court found in favor of the city and dismissed the complaint. The court vacated the trial court's judgment, holding that the trial court erred by dismissing the complaint without a declaration of the rights of the parties. However, the court ruled that the ordinance, which was designed to remove slums and blight from the city, did not violate the advertiser's First Amendment rights because it was narrowly tailored and furthered an important or substantial governmental interest. The court also ruled that the ordinance was properly enacted.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment in favor of the city, in the advertiser's declaratory judgment action. The court remanded the case to the trial court for an entry of a decree declaring the rights of the parties in accordance with the views expressed by the court.

Moss v. Director, Patuxent Institution


No. 88, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 561; 369 A.2d 1011; 1977 Md. LEXIS 921



March 2, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Fairbanks, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed. Case remanded to that court with directions that it reverse the order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County and remand the case to that court with instructions to dismiss the defective delinquent proceedings. Costs to be paid by Montgomery County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individual sought review of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed a trial court's order adjudging petitioner to be a defective delinquent and directing that he be remanded to the custody of an institution for defective delinquents for an indeterminate period.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pleaded guilty to two robbery charges and one escape charge, and he was sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment. Pursuant to the Defective Delinquent Act (Act), the trial court ordered that petitioner be transferred to an institution for an examination to ascertain whether he was a defective delinquent. The institution issued a report finding that petitioner was a defective delinquent. A jury later determined that petitioner was a defective delinquent. The trial court entered an order to that effect and directed that petitioner be returned to the institution. The appellate court affirmed. The court reversed, holding that a statutory prerequisite to institutionalization was not complied with and, therefore, that petitioner was entitled to be released from the institution. The court noted that under § 8(a) of the Act, the trial court was required to "forthwith" summon petitioner to appear before it following the issuance of the institution's report to advise petitioner of the results and his rights under the Act. The court determined that the four-month delay between the issuance of the report and the hearing violated petitioner's right to a prompt hearing under § 8(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, which affirmed a trial court's order adjudging petitioner to be a defective delinquent, and remanded the matter to the appellate court with instructions that it remand the matter to the trial court for dismissal of the defective delinquent proceedings.

Free State Realty Co. v. Baltimore


No. 71, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 550; 369 A.2d 1030; 1977 Md. LEXIS 920



March 2, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Court of Common Pleas of Baltimore City, Murphy, James W., J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed a decision of a trial court in favor of appellees, a mayor and city council, in a condemnation proceeding. The trial court found that it was necessary for the city to acquire immediate possession and title to the property and that the necessity was not due to any substantial fault or neglect on the part of the city.


OVERVIEW: The city filed a petition to condemn the leasehold property for urban renewal purposes. On the same day, it filed a petition for immediate possession, paying into the trial court an amount equal to the estimated fair market value of the property in question. The city attached an affidavit explaining the deterioration of the property, which was a menace to the public health, and reciting that the owner had failed to correct the deterioration. The court held that the city had authority to acquire the property under Md. Const. art. XI-B, § 1; Md. Const. art. III, § 40A; 1949 Md. Laws 217; Baltimore City, Md., Code Pub. Loc. Laws § 21-16 (1972); and Baltimore, Md., Ordinance No. 152, § 26. The administrative officers had necessary discretion to ascertain specific facts upon which a prescribed application of the police power was made to depend. The uses contemplated were public uses. The court concluded that the record was devoid of any allegation or implication of improper motive or purpose on the part of the city and that the city made out a prima facie case in the evidence presented by it which established a sufficient basis for the city's entering into immediate possession.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

430 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Residential Industrial Loan Co. v. Weinberg


No. 120, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 483; 369 A.2d 563; 1977 Md. LEXIS 916



February 24, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Frosh, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County affirmed in part and reversed in part and case remanded to that court for entry of an order as herein stated. Costs to be paid by Manuel M. Weinberg and Rex L. Sturm, trustees, and Frederick Contractors, Inc. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the holder of a deed of trust, and the holder of a mechanics' lien, sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which determined the ordering of priorities among three real property lien creditors of a bankrupt corporation. Appellee was the holder of a deed of trust that was given first priority.


OVERVIEW: The holder of a mechanics' lien performed work for a corporation that went bankrupt. Before the work was completed, the bankrupt corporation obtained a permanent first trust loan from the first holder of a deed of trust. The deed of trust was duly recorded. The holder of the mechanics' lien was never paid. It filed a mechanics' lien against the property owned by the bankrupt, recorded the instrument, and filed a complaint to foreclose its lien. Before the foreclosure proceedings could be terminated, the bankrupt corporation obtained another loan from the second holder of a deed of trust, secured by a second deed of trust, which was duly recorded. The bankrupt corporation demanded arbitration with the holder of the mechanics' lien, and a dispute, which lasted for years, ensued over whether arbitration was required before the mechanics' lien could be foreclosed. The second deed of trust was recorded after the holder of the mechanics' lien's bill of complaint to foreclose, but prior to any judicial determination of the issue. The court held that because the mechanics' lien was not established until after the recordation of the deeds of trust, it was junior in priority to both of them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and the case was remanded for entry of an order indicating that the mechanics' lien was third in priority. Costs were to be paid by the holder of the mechanics' lien. First priority was to the holder of the deed of trust that was recorded first. Second priority went to the holder of the deed of trust that was recorded second. Third priority went to the holder of the mechanics' lien.

Governor of Md. v. Exxon Corp.


No. 10, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 410; 370 A.2d 1102; 1977 Md. LEXIS 912; 1977-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P61,297



February 18, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
 Motion for Stay of Mandate Filed March 17, 3 Motions for Reconsideration Filed March 18 and 1 March 21, 1977; All Motions Denied April 13, 1977, See Opinion by Eldridge, J., at 456. Notice of Appeal to Supreme Court of United States Filed June 23, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Childs, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County reversed, and case remanded to that court for entry of a judgment in accordance with this opinion. Appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oil companies filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment that Md. Ann. Code art. 56, § 157E was unconstitutional and an injunction prohibiting its enforcement. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) ruled that the act was unconstitutional and issued the requested injunction, and the state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted Md. Ann. Code art. 56, § 157E, which prohibited the operation of retail service stations by producers and refiners of petroleum. The oil companies claimed that the legislation was unconstitutional because it violated numerous provisions of the state and federal constitutions. The court ruled that the challenged legislation was constitutional. In so holding, the court found that (1) the legislation did not violate substantive due process because it was not arbitrary, oppressive, or unreasonable; (2) the legislation did not violate the Commerce Clause because it did not discriminate against out-of-state economic interests and because the state's interest outweighed any burden imposed on interstate commerce; (3) there was no Takings Clause violation because the oil companies were not deprived of all beneficial use of their property; (4) the legislation did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because its classification scheme bore a rational relationship to the objective of preserving competition within the retail gasoline industry; and (5) the legislation was not invalid under the Supremacy Clause because it was not inconsistent with federal law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court and remanded the case with instructions to enter a judgment upholding the constitutionality of the legislation.

Mazor v. State, Dep't of Correction


No. 31, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 355; 369 A.2d 82; 1977 Md. LEXIS 907



February 8, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Harford County, Close, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellant to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public employee sought review from a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the circuit court's interpreting Md. Code Ann. art. 101, § 33, to apply to the facts presented in the case and holding that the statute was constitutional. Appellant had applied for workmen's compensation benefits. Appellees, Department of Corrections, State Accident Fund, and Subsequent Injury Fund, opposed the application.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, employed as a penitentiary guard with the Department of Corrections, suffered severe injuries when he was stabbed and beaten during an incident at a correctional facility. Unable to return to work, appellant thereafter retired. Having determined that appellant was totally and permanently incapacitated for duty as a result of his injury, the Employees' Retirement System of the State of Maryland, Md. Code Ann. art. 73B, §§ 1-3, awarded him, effective upon his retirement, an accidental disability pension. Appellant also applied for workmen's compensation benefits. Appellees claimed that pursuant to Md. Code Ann. art. 101, § 33, award of the pension discharged their obligation to provide workmen's compensation benefits. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision, holding that art. 101, § 33 entitled the insurer, as well as the employer, to a discharge of its obligation. The court further held that art. 101, § 33 discharged the workmen's compensation obligation when the employee's injury did not result in death. Moreover, the court found that the statute infringed on none of appellant's rights and was thus constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court denying appellant's application for workmen's compensation benefits.

Gayety Books, Inc. v. Baltimore


No. 101, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 206; 369 A.2d 581; 1977 Md. LEXIS 893



January 24, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Grady, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; appellants to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, defendant adult bookstore owners sought review of the judgments of the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland) that granted plaintiff city's motions for summary judgment as to the issue of defendants' liability for the payment of annual license fees for coin-operated amusement devices required by Baltimore, Md., City Code art. 15, § 71 (1966).


OVERVIEW: The summary judgements in the city's favor were based upon a decision entered by a federal court in a declaratory judgment action that the owners had filed challenging the constitutionality of § 71. The federal court held that § 71 was constitutional on its face and as applied, and that the city was entitled to apply a non-regulatory, non-confiscatory license tax on all coin-operated amusement devices to coin-operated movie machines. The court granted certiorari and affirmed the trial court's judgments. In so doing, the court followed the reasoning of the federal court and its conclusion. The court held that the fact that the number of devices in question was for determination by the trier of fact did not preclude the grant of summary judgment as to liability. Whether such devices were within the contemplation of § 71 was a matter of statutory construction. The trial court was correct in finding that there was no genuine dispute as to a material fact with respect to the necessity of obtaining a license and that the city was entitled to judgment as a matter of law with respect to the owners' liability for payment of the fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

Maryland Action for Foster Children, Inc. v. State


No. 5, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 133; 367 A.2d 491; 1977 Md. LEXIS 888



January 7, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed February 4, 1977; Denied February 18, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; Turnbull, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Petitioners to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an association and foster parents, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) that sustained, without leave to amend, the demurrer filed by defendants, the State of Maryland and its officials, in plaintiffs' action that sought a writ of mandamus ordering defendants to pay all foster parents no less than the minimum sum mandated by Md. Ann. Code art. 88A, § 60B(b) (1969, Cum. Supp. 1976).


OVERVIEW: In sustaining defendants' demurrer to plaintiff's petition for mandamus, the trial court held that § 60B, relating to the foster care program administered by the social services administration, was unconstitutional as an invalid appropriation bill, but that it had, in effect, the same weight and value as a joint resolution of the state legislature. On appeal, the only relief sought by plaintiffs was an order requiring the governor to comply with § 60B (b) "in the preparation of all future budgets." The court held that § 60B(b) was a constitutional statute, setting forth valid criteria for the administration of a particular government program. However, the court concluded that pursuant to the provisions of the Budget Amendment found in Md. Const. art. III, § 52, and the purposes underlying those provisions, that the funding of Md. Ann. Code art. 88A, § 60B(b) in future annual budgets was a matter constitutionally committed to the governor's discretion. Assuming that no other constitutional principle was violated, the court held that the judiciary had no authority to control the governor's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Morrell v. Williams


No. 62, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


279 Md. 497; 366 A.2d 1040; 1976 Md. LEXIS 580



December 8, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion Reaffirmed February 28, 1977. Limited Reargument Granted, Hearing Held and The Opinion of The Court Reaffirmed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Three appeals in one record from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Ross, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for $ 20,000.00 in favor of Sylvia Hall Williams as personal representative against Morris A. Morrell reversed, without a new trial. Judgment for $ 20,000.00 in favor of Sylvia Hall Williams as personal representative against John Lee Worsham affirmed. Judgment for $ 30,000.00 in favor of Sylvia Hall Williams against Morris A. Morrell reversed without a new trial. Judgment for $ 30,000.00 in favor of Sylvia Hall Williams against John Lee Worsham reversed, and case remanded for trial on issue of damages only. Judgment for $ 20,000.00 in favor of Raynetta Renee Fowlkes against John Lee Worsham reversed without a new trial. Costs to be paid, one-third by Sylvia Hall Williams; one-third by John Lee Worsham and one-third by Raynetta Renee Fowlkes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, decedent's mother and child. filed a wrongful death action against defendants, van driver and his employer, after the van struck and killed the decedent. The trial court sustained the employer's demurrer on the child's count. The jury found the driver and the employer liable on the other counts. The driver, the employer, and the child appealed. The court granted certiorari before the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) heard the case.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was struck and killed by a van owned by the employer. The decedent's mother filed a wrongful death action against the driver and the employer. More than two years after the decedent's death, the mother amended the declaration to include a claim for her mental anguish. Later, a count was added on behalf of the decedent's infant child. The trial court sustained the employer's demurrer on the child's count. A jury eventually imposed liability on the driver for negligence and on the employer for negligent entrustment and awarded the mother and the child damages. The employer, the driver, and the child appealed. The court granted certiorari and reversed holding that there was insufficient evidence of negligent entrustment to go to the jury because the driver misrepresented to the employer that he had a valid driver's license and was an experienced driver. The court found that the amended declarations for the mother's mental anguish and on behalf of the child stated new causes of action and were barred by the two-year statute of limitations under Md. Ann. Code art. 67, § 4(a) (1957 & Repl. Vol. 1970). The court affirmed the awards to the mother for the driver's negligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the awards to the decedent's mother for the driver's negligence, but reversed the child's damage award and the damage award to the mother for the employer's negligent entrustment. The court remanded the case.
