Shell Oil Co. v. Supervisor of Assessments


No. 73, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 659; 366 A.2d 369; 1976 Md. LEXIS 663



December 7, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Taylor, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oil company sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) that affirmed the determination by respondent assessment supervisor that land owned by the oil company was assessed at a value that took into consideration that it was suitable for a service station, which occupied the land during the years for which the land was assessment.


OVERVIEW: The oil company claimed that all real property was to be assessed and taxed within the same classification or subclassification and must be treated uniformly; the assessment supervisor had not treated the land equally in his assessment with comparable land in the area; and that the assessment was discriminator. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that affirmed the assessment supervisor's evaluation of the oil company's land and held that a number of factors were considered in assessing the value of the land, which was required to be assessed at the time for which the tax was being imposed. The court further held that the evidence showed that factors were considered regarding the land value, including the use of the land as a location for a service station, and that the assessment supervisor's evaluation of the land was not discriminatory, which required the oil company to show that the evaluation was tainted by fraud or an intentional underevaluation of other property in the area that was similar to the oil company's tract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that affirmed the evaluation of the oil company's land by the assessment supervisor, which was based on the condition of the land during the year for which the land was assessed for tax purposes.

Cooper v. Wicomico County, Dep't of Public Works


No. 8, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 596; 366 A.2d 55; 1976 Md. LEXIS 659



November 30, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County; Pollitt, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded without affirmance or reversal for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Costs to abide the result.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), which upheld a decision by a workmen's compensation commission ordering the employer to pay appellee employee a supplemental award in addition to the benefits he was already receiving.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained an accidental injury in the course of his employment with the county, his employer. A workmen's compensation commission found the employee to be totally and permanently disable and ordered weekly compensation benefits. Several years later, a statute was passed, 1973 Md. Laws, ch. 832, § 36(10), which permitted employees that were permanently and totally disabled a supplemental allowance. The employer was ordered by the commission to comply with the mandate of the new law and to increase the weekly payments made to the employee. On appeal, the trial court accepted the county's argument that the new statute could not be applied retrospectively and ruled that it was unconstitutional and invalid. Upon review, the court held that the trial court was correct in finding that the operational effect of the statute required it to pay more than it was required to pay under the law in effect at the time of the injury. Nonetheless, the court remanded the case for a determination of the merits as to whether the supplemental payments required under the new statute would so deplete a subsequent injury fund as to required that additional assessments be made.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case without affirmance or reversal for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

438 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Downs v. State


No. 27, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 610; 366 A.2d 41; 1976 Md. LEXIS 660



November 30, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for St. Mary's County, Mattingly, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirming the conviction for disorderly conduct reversed; case remanded to that Court with instructions to remand it to the Circuit Court for St. Mary's County for a new trial; costs to be paid by the County Commissioners of St. Mary's County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the trial court's judgment that had convicted defendant of disorderly conduct in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 123(c) (1957, Repl. Vol. 1976), resisting arrest, and assault and battery.


OVERVIEW: A state trooper overheard defendant's loud remarks containing vulgar language and a racial slur while in a restaurant. The trial court convicted defendant of disorderly conduct, and the appellate court affirmed the conviction. On further appeal, the court reversed. After reviewing the development of the "fighting" words doctrine, the court concluded that defendant's first remark referring to police officers did not constitute "fighting" words because the state trooper, a possible addressee, was not aroused by the comment. Examining defendant's second statement that "The fucking niggers in this county are no better than goddamn policemen," the court concluded that based on precedent the use of the adjective "fucking" was not punishable in the absence of compelling reasons. The court found that the remainder of the remark was made by defendant during a conversation with friends and there was no evidence that anyone who might have heard it was so aroused as to respond in a violent manner. Thus, defendant's remarks were not the kind of personally abusive epithets that fell outside of the protection of the First Amendment. The court held that defendant engaged in protected speech.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, which had affirmed defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct, resisting arrest, and assault and battery. The court remanded the case with instructions to remand it to the trial court for a new trial.

Blackwell v. State


No. 45, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 466; 365 A.2d 545; 1976 Md. LEXIS 649



November 9, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Criminal Court of Baltimore; Dorf, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: As to the murder indictments: judgments affirmed except as to the sentences of death; death sentences vacated; case remanded to the Criminal Court of Baltimore for imposition of life sentences consistent with this opinion. As to the arson indictment: judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court of Baltimore (Maryland), which imposed death under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 413 after defendant, an arsonist whose fire had killed six people, was convicted of first-degree murder. In seeking review, defendant sought reversal based on art. 27, § 413's constitutionality, the absence of instructions on a lesser degree of homicide, and rulings concerning opening and closing statements.


OVERVIEW: After a fire set by defendant killed six people, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 413(b), (d). Accordingly, review was sought, and the court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence. In vacating the sentence, the court held art. 27, § 413(b), (d) was unconstitutional because it lacked guidelines enabling the sentencing authority to consider mitigating factors. Based on its holding, the court remanded with instructions to impose life sentences under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 413(a), because the unconstitutional sentence had not affected the conviction and art. 27, § 413(a) had been severable from the unconstitutional provisions. In affirming, the court rejected the contention that instructions on a lesser degree of homicide had been required because murder committed during arson was first degree murder, rather than second degree murder, and there was no evidence to support a lesser offense. Finally, the court held defendant's opening had been improper because it had encouraged the jury to disregard the law, while the prosecution's closing had not been improper because it had been argument in response.


OUTCOME: Although the court vacated defendant's death sentence based on the death penalty statute's unconstitutionality, the court remanded for the imposition of life sentences after affirming defendant's conviction for first-degree murder, notwithstanding the absence of instructions on a lesser degree of homicide and rulings concerning opening and closing statements.

Phipps v. General Motors Corp.


Misc. No. 6, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 337; 363 A.2d 955; 1976 Md. LEXIS 635; 20 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 312



September 29, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certification of Question of Law from the United States District Court for the District of Maryland; Miller, J.



DISPOSITION: Questions of law answered as herein set forth. Appellee to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was before the court on certification of questions of law by the United States District Court for the District of Maryland involving plaintiffs' claim of damages based upon strict liability and resulting from defendant's breach of warranties and causing loss of consortium, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Com. Law §§ 2-714 and 2-715.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff husband, who was in the automobile service industry, crashed an automobile into a tree while he was test driving it. Following his injury, plaintiff and his wife brought action against the manufacturer of the automobile alleging that the accident occurred when the accelerator became stuck without warning due to latent defects in some of its components. Plaintiffs based their claims on strict liability, and on breach of express warranties. Defendant denied the claims and filed motions to dismiss because strict liability was not appropriate in the circumstance and that an action for loss of consortium could not be brought by a non-buyer. The court held that plaintiff husband who was injured by a defective and unreasonably dangerous product would succeed in making the seller of the product, who was in a better position to take precautions and protect against defect, bear the loss, on a theory of strict liability. Furthermore, the court held that joint action for loss of consortium would succeed when defendant's conduct amounted to a breach of warranty.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant was liable both in strict liability and for breach of warranty.

Harford County v. Tatar, Lininger, Clark & Wood, Inc.

September 28, 1976, Decided

DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and case remanded for passage of an order in conformity with this opinion; Harford County to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant architectural firm sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland), which found that two bills pertaining to the procurement of contracts were invalid and held in favor of appellees, a county executive and related parties.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between a county executive and a county council regarding the expansion of a courthouse and a related contract with an architectural firm. A county council adopted two bills regarding the procurement of contracts. The county executive vetoed both bills, and the council overrode his vetoes. The executive, thereafter, entered into a contract on behalf of the county with the architectural firm. The issues went before the trial court, which found that both the bills were invalid because they violated the principle of separation of powers. Upon review, the court held that it was unable to decide the issues before it and remanded the case for the passage of an order dismissing the bill of complaint without prejudice to the bringing of any proper proceeding by the architect for compensation alleged to be due it or by the taxpayers of the county for construction of the bills. The court stated that there was no authority before it for a suit brought in the corporate name of a political subdivision where the conflicting officers joined in the petition and asked the courts to determine the controversy between them. Such matters were usually resolved in taxpayers' suits.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for passage of an order in conformity with its opinion.

Perkins v. Eskridge


No. 65, September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 619; 366 A.2d 21; 1976 Md. LEXIS 661



September 24, 1976  
December 1, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Sodaro, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a malpractice action, petitioners wife and husband sought review of an order of the Baltimore City Court (Maryland), which granted the respondent doctor's Md. Code Ann. § 6-204 motion for removal.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed a medical malpractice action against respondents in municipal court, and respondents filed a motion for removal to a jurisdiction outside the city, pursuant to Md. Code Ann. § 6-204. The trial court granted the motion, and petitioners sought review. They contended that the removal statute was unconstitutional. The court reversed. It found that even though Md. Const. art. IV, § 8, which proscribed legislative enactments related to removal, had been partially found unconstitutional in a prior decision, it was still valid in part. The court further found that statute violated the valid portions of Md. Const. art. IV, § 8, because the legislature exceeded its authority. The court held that the only method by which the legislature could provide for removal to some other county or judicial circuit would be to amend the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's removal order and found that the removal statute was unconstitutional.

Folly Farms I, Inc. v. Trustees of Clients' Sec. Trust Fund of The Bar

444 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Evans


No. 173, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 197; 362 A.2d 629; 1976 Md. LEXIS 621



July 15, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Munger, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for murder in the second degree. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed defendant's conviction, holding that the jury instructions violated the constitution because they had placed the burden of proof of mitigating circumstances on defendant. The court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the reversal of defendant's conviction for murder in the second degree. The jury instructions to the effect that malice could be presumed from pointing a deadly weapon at a vital part of the body unconstitutionally relieved the state of its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt the absence of mitigation where a jury had returned a conviction for murder in the second degree and the defense of provocation had been fairly raised. While it might have been proper to infer an intention to kill or to do grievous bodily harm from the directing of a deadly weapon at a vital part of the human anatomy, it was improper to infer "malice" therefrom, since the use of deadly force did not itself negate the absence of mitigating circumstances. Otherwise, the state would have been unconstitutionally relieved of its burden of proving the absence of mitigation and the burden of persuasion would have shifted to defendant to lower his guilt to manslaughter. Due process of law was offended by placing the burden on the defendant to prove, by any standard, the existence of mitigating circumstances necessary to lower a felonious homicide to the level of manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Gordon v. Commissioners of St. Michaels


No. 1 (Adv.), September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 128; 359 A.2d 543; 1976 Md. LEXIS 615



July 12, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Talbot County; Clark, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed and case remanded for passage of a decree conforming to this opinion; costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant opponents sought review of the decree of the Circuit Court for Talbot County (Maryland), which entered a judgment on the issue of the constitutionally of Md. Code art. 66B, § 4.05(d) for appellees, members of the Planning Commission of St. Michaels (Maryland) and an inn owner, holding that the incorporated town was constitutionally empowered under art. 66B, § 4.05(d) to zone all lands lying within one mile of its corporate boundaries.


OVERVIEW: The opponents took exception to a change made by the commissioners relative to zoning in the area around an inn, which was not within the town's corporate limits but was within one mile of its corporate boundaries. The opponents sought a declaratory judgment that Md. Code art. 66B, § 4.05(d) was unconstitutional as far as it purported to confer upon the commissioners the power to zone land lying outside the town's corporate boundaries. The chancellor found that § 4.05(d) was constitutional. On appeal, the court noted that § 4.05(d) concerned only Talbot County. Because there was only one class of municipal corporations in Maryland and because Md. Const. art. XI-E, § 1 specified that the power of the general assembly to act relative to the affairs of municipal corporations was only by general, not specific, laws, it followed that § 4.05(d) was unconstitutional. However, from the very nature of 1970 Md. Laws 672 the court concluded that the general assembly would have enacted it even had it known that Md. Code art. 66B, § 4.05(d) was invalid. Thus, the court separated from 1970 Md. Laws 672 only the portion purporting to grant special powers to the municipalities of Talbot County.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decree. The case was remanded for passage of a decree conforming to the court's opinion.

Secretary of Transp. v. Mancuso


No. 7 (Adv.), September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 81; 359 A.2d 79; 1976 Md. LEXIS 610



June 24, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Evans, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Secretary of the Maryland Department of Transportation, challenged the decree of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which found in favor of appellee citizens in the citizens' action to declare unconstitutional within the meaning of Md. Const. art. III, § 34 certain bonds issued by the Secretary. The Secretary argued that he was improperly enjoined from seeking approval for the sale of the bonds.


OVERVIEW: Under the authority of Md. Ann. Code art. 94A, §§ 1 to 11A (Supp. 1975), the Secretary authorized the issuance of bonds whose last serial principal maturity was later than 15 years from the date of issue. The citizens filed an action claiming that the bond issuance violated Md. Const. art. III, § 34 because it created debt that would not be discharged within 15 years from the time it was incurred. The trial court found in favor of the citizens, holding that the imposition, levy, and irrevocable pledge of tax revenues made the bonds "debt" in the constitutional sense contemplated by § 34, notwithstanding the statement in Md. Ann. Code art. 94A, § 9(d) that consolidated transportation bonds did not constitute a pledge of the faith and credit of the State of Maryland. The Secretary appealed, and the court affirmed. The true test of the special fund doctrine was not what came out of the fund, but what went in. The State had undertaken to provide part of the fund from a tax, so the bonds issued on the credit of the fund were in truth debts of the State. This use of the taxing authority for debt service payment for the bonds created a constitutional "debt" of the State.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decree.

 

447 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Baltimore Gas & Electric Co. v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 11 (Adv.), September Term, 1976


Court of Appeals of Maryland


278 Md. 26; 358 A.2d 241; 1976 Md. LEXIS 604



June 1, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Calvert County; Bowen, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; remanded for entry of a judgment conformable to the views expressed herein; appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Calvert County (Maryland), which denied the taxpayer's petition to declare a real property tax ordinance unconstitutional and declare that appellee Board of County Commissioners for Calvert County had exceeded its authority under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 48(b) to grant discounts to a real property tax. The taxpayer sought injunctive relief from the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The Board's tax ordinance granted tax discounts based on the size of the real property tax bill. The recipients of the highest benefit were individual owners whose property was subject to residential or agricultural use. Owners of commercial properties received almost no benefit. The taxpayer was an electrical utility company that owned a large amount of commercial property. Its tax payment compromised 60 percent of the taxes levied. The taxpayer filed a petition to invalidate the ordinance. The parties stipulated to the relevant facts, and the trial court denied the taxpayer's claim for relief. On appeal, the taxpayer challenged the ordinance on the grounds that the statutory purpose of § 48(b) was to encourage the prompt payment of taxes and that the ordinance served the purpose of alleviating the property tax burden on individuals with low or moderate incomes. The court agreed that the tax discounts established under the ordinance were not authorized by § 48(b). The Board's redistribution of the property tax burden was not authorized by § 48 or any other statute. The ordinance did not serve the legislative intention to induce the prompt payment of taxes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that denied the taxpayer's petition. The court held that the ordinance was invalid. The court remanded the taxpayer's petition to the trial court for the entry of judgment.

State v. Ensor


No. 102, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


277 Md. 529; 356 A.2d 259; 1976 Md. LEXIS 984



April 19, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed May 5, 1976; Denied May 21, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Grady, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded to the Court of Special Appeals for further remand to the Criminal Court of Baltimore for further proceedings consistent with this opinion; appellees to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, which reversed the denial of defendants' motion to dismiss an indictment returned by the grand jury and found that an assistant attorney general who was sworn in as a special assistant state's attorney (special prosecutor) under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 2-102(a) (1974) was not authorized to appear before the grand jury. The court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted by the grand jury for conspiracy to violate the false pretense laws, forgery, and attempts to obtain money under false pretenses. All of the charges arose out of alterations made in change orders relating to state construction contracts. The special prosecutor was sworn in as a special assistant state's attorney by the Criminal Court of Baltimore under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 2-102(a) (1974). The special prosecutor was not present during any deliberations or voting by the grand jury and there was no claim that the special prosecutor's presence before the grand jury resulted in any actual prejudice to defendants. Defendants argued that the special prosecutor was not qualified to appear before the grand jury. The court reversed the dismissal of the indictment and held that when the special prosecutor was appointed for the purpose of appearing before the grand jury in connection with the presentation of evidence relative to violations by defendants, his appointment was "in a specific proceeding" within the purview of § 2-102(a). The court held that Md. Const. art. V, § 9 did not apply because the appointment was not made by the state's attorney.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed defendants' indictments issued by the grand jury, held that the special prosecutor was lawfully qualified to appear before the grand jury, and remanded the action for trial and further proceedings.

Harden v. Mass Transit Administration


No. 92, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


277 Md. 399; 354 A.2d 817; 1976 Md. LEXIS 976



April 9, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland. Superior Court of Baltimore City, Grady, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirmed; appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant passengers sought review of declaratory judgment of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland holding that appellee mass transit administration was not statutorily required to maintain hospitalization, medical, and disability insurance for the benefit of appellant passengers.


OVERVIEW: Appellant passengers sought review of declaratory judgment holding that appellee mass transit administration was not statutorily required to maintain hospitalization, medical, and disability insurance for the benefit of appellant passengers. The court held that Md. Ann. Code art. 48A, § 539 et seq. and Md. Ann. Code art. 66 1/2, § 7-101 et seq., did not apply to appellee mass transit administration because the state General Assembly did not demonstrate any manifest intention to include appellee mass transit administration within those no fault and liability insurance provisions. Furthermore, if General Assembly had so intended it would have made specific provision to that effect. The court also held that due process rights of appellant passengers were not violated when General Assembly excluded appellee mass transit administration from requirements of mandatory no fault and liability insurance statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed declaratory judgment because General Assembly did not express intention to subject appellee mass transit administration to no fault and liability insurance requirements and if it had intended it would have made provision to that effect; exclusion from insurance requirements not violation of appellant passengers' equal protection rights.

 

450 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Anne Arundel County v. McDonough


No. 4, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


277 Md. 271; 354 A.2d 788; 1976 Md. LEXIS 967



March 9, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Wray, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; costs to be paid by the appellant, cross-appellee, Anne Arundel County, Maryland.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county officials challenged an order by the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which declared the result of a referendum vote on zoning of property within the county to be a nullity and of no effect, and ordered the county to proceed administratively in accordance with the ordinance as enacted.


OVERVIEW: The county officials claimed that the that § 308, Art. III of the Charter of Anne Arundel County was unconstitutional, as contrary to the provisions of the Constitution of Maryland, because the ballot was fatally flawed, as was the process in which it was enacted. The court agreed that the referendum on Question D was a nullity and of no effect. The county purportedly acted pursuant to statutory authority when it prepared the form and contents of the referendum question and certified it to the supervisors. However, the court held that such a referendum was limited to the amendments to the newly enacted re-zoning ordinance, and without recitation of the provisions, the proposed ballot question was not in accordance with the requirements of the statute and was fatally defective. The failure of the ballot question to present a clear, unambiguous, and understandable statement of the full and complete nature of the issues included in Question D constituted a deviation from the prescribed forms of the law, and the court affirmed the lower court's order nullifying the referendum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, and it ordered the county officials to pay for the costs of the appeal. The court held that because the referendum process was not followed, and because the notice requirements for special elections were not followed, the referendum was void.

 

451 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wooten


No. 87, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


277 Md. 114; 352 A.2d 829; 1976 Md. LEXIS 954



March 2, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland. Circuit Court for Baltimore County, Raine, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirmed. Costs to be paid by Baltimore County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought review of an order of the Court of Special Appeals Maryland that ruled that the action of the circuit court in suspending a portion of the life sentence of defendant after her conviction for murder in the first degree was permissible.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree for the murder of her husband. Although the court meted out life imprisonment, which it characterized as the mandatory sentence, it suspended the serving of all but the first eight years. The state objected, contending that the court was without authority to suspend any portion of the term, and brought a motion, pursuant to Md. R. App. & Other Jud. Rev. in Cir. Ct. 764a, to correct what it asserted was an illegal sentence. The motion was denied. The court of special appeals ruled that the action was permissible. The court of appeals affirmed and held that Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 641A (1957, 1971 Repl. Vol.), in clear, unambiguous, and unqualified language, bestowed upon courts the power to suspend completely or partially any and all sentences over which they had jurisdiction. Consequently, unless limited by some other provision of law, § 641A plainly permitted the court to suspend the mandatory life sentence of defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of special appeals was affirmed.

 

452 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Barry Properties v. Fick Bros. Roofing Co.


No. 62, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


277 Md. 15; 353 A.2d 222; 1976 Md. LEXIS 948



February 10, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed March 10, 1976; Denied March 19, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; Haile, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County affirmed. Appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) concluded that defendant landowner was not deprived of due process in connection with plaintiff subcontractor's mechanics' lien, determined that the subcontractor's lien was valid, and appointed a trustee to sell the landowner's property if the lien was not paid within 30 days. The landowner appealed, and the court granted certiorari while the appeal was pending.


OVERVIEW: The landowner contracted with a general contractor for the erection of a building on the landowner's property. The subcontractor contracted with the general contractor, agreeing to construct the building's roof. The subcontractor fully performed its obligations and was owed payment by the general contractor. The subcontractor gave the landowner notice of its intent to claim a mechanics' lien prior to filing the mechanics' lien and a bill of complaint to enforce the lien. The landowner sought summary judgment, arguing that Maryland's lien statute unconstitutionally deprived it of its property without procedural due process of law. On appeal, the landowner again argued that the lien statute deprived owners of their property without procedural due process, in contravention of Article 23 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights (Article 23) and the Fourteenth Amendment. The appellate court partially agreed with the landowner and held that certain provisions of the lien statute were unconstitutional. Nevertheless, the court concluded that the landowner was afforded due process prior to being deprived of its property through the enforcement proceedings at the trial court level.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decree.

 

453 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Erbe v. State


No. 39, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


276 Md. 541; 350 A.2d 640; 1976 Md. LEXIS 1103



January 7, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Sklar, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for certiorari review of the denial by the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, Criminal Court of Baltimore, of his post-conviction motion to dismiss his housebreaking and theft convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought certiorari review of a judgment which affirmed the denial of a motion to dismiss for lack of speedy sentencing. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that even under the assumption that the sentence was part of the trial for Sixth Amendment purposes, the delay between the time of filing the motion for a new trial and the denial of the motion was not a violation of defendants' speedy trial guarantee. The court observed that defendant did not request sentencing in the intervening period and as a result he was deemed to have waived any rights conferred upon him. The court further explained that the presumptive prejudice which arises from an inordinate delay in bringing a man to trial did not present the same question as prejudice after the conviction and any such inordinate delay was merely one of the factors to be considered in the balancing test. The court found no denial of due process or the right to speedy trial was shown because the inordinate sentencing delay was entirely inadvertent on the state's part, no steps to request sentencing were taken, and no prejudice from either confinement or disappearing witnesses was sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied defendant's motion to dismiss his housebreaking and theft convictions.

 

454 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Yates


No. 68, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


276 Md. 475; 348 A.2d 837; 1975 Md. LEXIS 740; 84 A.L.R.3d 1



December 22, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed January 20, 1976; Denied February 5, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Childs, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree modified as set forth in the foregoing opinion, and as modified, affirmed; mandate to issue forthwith; costs of this appeal to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state and appellee/cross-appellant resident sought review after the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) held that the State Prosecutor Act, which created the office of state prosecutor within the office of the attorney general, was constitutional, with certain exceptions, and that the unconstitutional provisions of the Act were severable.


OVERVIEW: The state prosecutor would be nominated by a selection commission created by the Act and appointed for a term of six years. The state prosecutor would investigate alleged criminal offenses on his own initiative or at the request of parties specified in the Act. The trial court held that the Act was constitutional except to the extent that it purported to designate the chief judges of the Court of Appeals, the Court of Special Appeals, and the District Court as ex officio members of the commission; those provisions, however, were severable. The court held that the state prosecutor's power to initiate an investigation and commence prosecution if a state's attorney did not act was a clear invasion of the state's attorney's most awesome discretionary power: to determine whether or not to prosecute. Further, the Act empowered the state prosecutor to represent the state in any appeal or postconviction proceeding, which invaded the attorney general's constitutional duty. In each instance, the Act transferred power from what had traditionally been an elected official to an appointed official. The result sought could only be achieved by a constitutional amendment.


OUTCOME: The court declared the State Prosecutor Act to be unconstitutional and void in its entirety.

 

455 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Westchester West No. 2 Ltd. Partnership v. Montgomery County


No. 32, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


276 Md. 448; 348 A.2d 856; 1975 Md. LEXIS 738



December 18, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; McAuliffe, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed. Appellants to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlords sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which denied the landlords' action to have appellee county's rent control ordinance declared unconstitutional as violating due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: The county's rent control ordinance generally limited rent increases to four percent of the base rent per year. Several landlords filed suit against the county seeking to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional on the ground that it constitutes a deprivation of property without due process of law in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The circuit court held that there was no exception to the general constitutionality analysis for rent control laws. The circuit court refused to find the ordinance unconstitutional. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The court held that there was a real and substantial relationship between the ordinance and the public health, safety, morals, and welfare of the community and therefore the ordinance did not violate due process. The court noted that the United States Supreme Court had upheld price control legislation under the Due Process Clause regardless of whether an emergency existed or whether the business was one affected with the public interest. The constitutionality of the ordinance did not depend on whether there was an emergency shortage of rental housing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that did not find the county rent control ordinance violative of the Due Process Clause.

Steuart Petroleum Co. v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 41, September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


276 Md. 435; 347 A.2d 854; 1975 Md. LEXIS 737



December 3, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for St. Mary's County; Powers, C. J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order and decree appealed from affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petroleum company challenged an order of the Circuit Court for St. Mary's County (Maryland), which upheld the revocation of a building permit for the petroleum company in a consolidated action by appellee county to enjoin the construction of a refinery by the petroleum company and the petroleum company's challenge of the revocation of the permit.


OVERVIEW: The company sought to build a refinery on its land, and obtained a building permit for a foundation pad for a utility area. Before construction began, an ordinance was enacted requiring construction to begin within four months of the permit. The county then revoked the permit because construction was not initiated in time. The county sought an injunction to prevent the construction of the refinery itself, on the basis that the Bailey Bill, Md. Ann. Code art. 66B, § 4.01(c), (1957, 1970 Repl. Vol., 1975 Cum. Supp.), which was enacted after the permit was issued, prohibited the use of land and buildings for refining of petroleum or petroleum products. The injunction and revocation actions were consolidated, and the trial court affirmed the revocation of the permit. The company appealed, and the court granted certiorari and affirmed, holding that the company had not timely initiated construction, and that the company's substantial expenditures preliminary to the commencement of construction did not create a vested right to continue under the building permit issued prior to a change in the zoning classification of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding the revocation of the building permit and upholding the validity of a statute prohibiting the construction of a refinery.

 

457 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Director, Patuxent Institution


No. 115, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


276 Md. 272; 347 A.2d 179; 1975 Md. LEXIS 728



November 7, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals from the Criminal Court of Baltimore; Karwacki, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the orders of the Criminal Court of Baltimore (Maryland), which adjudged them in civil contempt of court and incarcerated them when they refused to cooperate with mental health officials in mental examinations to determine whether they were "defective delinquents" within the meaning of Maryland Ann. Code art. 31B, §5 (1957).


OVERVIEW: The trial court held defendants in contempt when they refused to cooperate with the staff of Patuxent Institution in mental examinations to determine whether they were "defective delinquents" within the meaning of art. 31B, § 5. Defendants sought review, and the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) the intent of the Defective Delinquent Act was to require confinement and treatment of those individuals who had been convicted of crime and who constituted an actual danger to society; (2) the psychological and psychiatric examinations were not accusatorial stages of a criminal proceeding and did not constitute "in-custody" interrogation under Miranda; (3) defective delinquency proceedings were civil in nature and because defendants' statements did not subject them to criminal liability, there was no constitutional infirmity in the manner in which the examination at Patuxent was conducted; (4) a person undergoing examination at Patuxent had no absolute right to remain silent; and (5) persons referred to Patuxent for examination constitutionally could be held in contempt for refusal to comply with an order requiring them to submit to and cooperate with the examination process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the criminal court that adjudged defendants in civil contempt of court and incarcerated them for refusing to cooperate with mental health officials in mental examinations to determine whether they were "defective delinquents."

Davidson v. Miller


No. 226, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


276 Md. 54; 344 A.2d 422; 1975 Md. LEXIS 713



September 18, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Carter, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in favor of Mildred Leggett, individually, against the petitioners, affirmed. Judgment in favor of Alenetta Miller, infant, reversed and the case, as it pertains to her claim against the petitioners, is remanded to the Baltimore City Court for a new trial restricted to a reassessment of damages. Costs to be paid equally by the petitioners and respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an automobile-pedestrian personal injury action, petitioners appealed from a decision of the Baltimore City Court (Maryland), which awarded respondent infant a sum in compensation for her injuries and awarded respondent mother a sum as reimbursement for expenses she incurred on behalf of respondent infant.


OVERVIEW: In an automobile-pedestrian personal injury action, the jury awarded respondent infant a sum as compensation for her injuries, and a sum to respondent mother as reimbursement for medical expenses she incurred on behalf of respondent infant. On appeal, petitioners asserted that a number of evidential and procedural errors were committed at the trial level. The court stated that evidence of prospective damages, as were awarded to respondent infant, had to be in terms of the certain or probable and not of the possible. The court held that it was error to receive into evidence a doctor's speculative opinion on the issue of respondent infant's potential problem in bearing children. Because this opinion was the only testimony on the subject, it followed that it was likewise error to permit abnormal childbirth complications to be considered by the jury in assessing damages. However, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to send the case outside of the city for trial. A judge who ordered removal of an action had discretion in determining the precise court within or without the circuit to which the case would be sent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of respondent mother, but reversed the judgment in favor of respondent infant and remanded the matter for the new trial restricted to a reassessment of damages.

 

459 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Shell Oil Co. v. Supervisor of Assessments


No. 246, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


276 Md. 36; 343 A.2d 521; 1975 Md. LEXIS 711



September 9, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Maryland Tax Court.



DISPOSITION: Case transferred to the Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Costs to abide the result. Mandate to issue forthwith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer appealed a decision from the Maryland Tax Court which affirmed the assessment of its business by respondent county Supervisor of Assessments.


OVERVIEW: The court ruled that it did not have jurisdiction to consider the appeal from a tax court decision. The tax court was found to be an administrative agency, created by the legislature. The legislature did not have state constitutional authority to create a new court. Since jurisdiction of both the Court of Appeals and the Court of Special Appeals was limited to review of judicial decisions, the legislature could not enact statutes which provided for those courts to have original jurisdiction over challenges to tax court decisions. Therefore, the court held that Ch. 385 of the Laws of 1971, which provided such original jurisdiction, was unconstitutional. Since its provisions were not severable, the court held it was invalid in its entirety. The court then considered the severability provisions of Ch. 448 of the Acts of 1975, and ruled that the circuit courts had original jurisdiction, with a right to appeal to the Court of Special Appeals, and that further review by the Court of Appeals would be by way of certiorari. Thus, it was proper for the court to transfer the case to the county circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case to the Prince George's County Circuit Court for judicial review of the tax assessment.

 

460 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Wiggins v. State


No. 185, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


275 Md. 689; 344 A.2d 80; 1975 Md. LEXIS 997



September 5, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland. Circuit Court of Baltimore City, James W. Murphy, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed for certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, which affirmed the denial of his bill of complaint, requesting a ruling that his convictions as an adult for burglary committed when he was 16 years old were a nullity in view of a later holding that the Maryland Juvenile Causes Act (Act), Md. Ann. Code art. 26, § 51 et seq., (1957, 1971 Repl. Vol.) was unconstitutional insofar as it exempted defendant from the Act.


OVERVIEW: In 1960, when defendant committed the burglaries, the Act exempted Baltimore City from the uniform juvenile age requirement of 18 years. In Baltimore City, where defendant committed the burglaries, a juvenile was defined as one under the age of 16 years. Because defendant was not quite 16 when he committed two of the six burglaries, the trial court waived defendant to the jurisdiction of the criminal court for those counts. About 10 years later, a decision was rendered finding that the Act insofar as it exempted Baltimore City from the uniform juvenile age requirement of 18 years was unconstitutional. Such holding was found to apply retrospectively. The court denied defendant relief and affirmed his convictions, finding that defendant's convictions were not contaminated to the extent that the new juvenile age requirement had to apply to his convictions retrospectively. The court noted that he was accorded the right to a jury trial and was entitled to the appointment of counsel. The court also balanced defendant's rights and fairness to society at large and held that it was unnecessary to apply the holding retrospectively and nullify defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions as an adult for a burglary that was committed when he was 16 years old.

 

461 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Slate v. Zitomer


No. 160, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


275 Md. 534; 341 A.2d 789; 1975 Md. LEXIS 985



July 14, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed August 12, 1975; Denied August 27, 1975. Certiorari Denied, Supreme Court of the United States, January 19, 1976; Sub Nom Gasperich v. Church.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Court of Special Appeals reversed. Cases remanded to the Court of Special Appeals with directions to affirm the judgments of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County and the Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Costs to be paid by respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, physicians and related individuals, sought review of an order of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, that reversed a trial court order granting their pleas of limitations in wrongful death actions under 1971 Md. Laws ch. 784, § 1. The trial court held that ch. 784, § 1 had not extended the limitations period to three years on plaintiffs' wrongful death actions that accrued in October and November of 1969.


OVERVIEW: The Act extending the statute of limitations for wrongful death actions provided that it was to be applied prospectively and retrospectively to be applied to any cause of action arising prior to 1968. The court of appeals determined that the Act also applied retroactively to causes of action arising after July 1, 1969, finding that a literal application of the statute would produce a bizarre result. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the statute clearly and unambiguously provided that it was applicable to causes of action that arose prior to July 1, 1968 and after July 1, 1971. The court noted that retroactive application of statutes was disfavored, particularly where substantive rights were involved. Since the wrongful death statute created a new liability not existing at common law, the court held that compliance with the period of limitations was a condition precedent to the right to maintain the action and retrospective application was only permitted if clearly expressed in the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision reversing the trial court's order that granted defendants' pleas of limitations.

 

462 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Pemberton v. Montgomery County


No. 205, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


275 Md. 363; 340 A.2d 240; 1975 Md. LEXIS 971



June 27, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Mitchell, J.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county granted appellee gas company a special permit to build a gas station. Appellant citizen claimed that the gas company failed to comply with the terms of the permit and that the operation of the gas station was unlawful. The county board (board) ruled that the construction was valid and complied with the permit. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) affirmed the board's order. The citizen sought review.


OVERVIEW: The citizen claimed that the lower court erroneously found that the gas company complied with the permit. The court rejected this claim and affirmed the lower court's judgment. The citizen claimed that the permit to build a retaining wall did not comply with the requirement for a building permit. The court held that a building permit was not limited to a permit for a building, per se, but included a permit for a portion of the building or project. In addition, the court found that the retaining wall was an indispensable part of the gasoline station. The court also rejected the claim that the gas company's work was merely preliminary and did not constitute the requisite commencement of construction. The court held that construction of the retaining wall was necessary and prerequisite to the construction of the rest of the gas station. The court further rejected the citizen's claim that work was not timely because it was done right before the period expired. The court found that the work could be performed at any time during the permit period and the fact that it was done towards the end of this period and during bad weather did not indicate bad faith or non-compliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that upheld the board's order permitting the operation of a gas station.

Prince George's County v. Chillum-Adelphi Volunteer Fire Dept., Inc.


No. 215, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


275 Md. 374; 340 A.2d 265; 1975 Md. LEXIS 972



June 27, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; McCullough, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree, as modified herein, affirmed; Prince George's County to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff volunteer fire companies and defendant county appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland). The volunteer companies sought declaratory relief after the county enacted Prince George's County, Md., Code of Public Local Laws § 32-17 and Prince George's Count, Md., Charter §14. In a previous appeal, the court remanded to the trial court for a determination of the constitutional issues presented.


OVERVIEW: The county contended that the volunteer companies were instrumentalities of the county and that the county fire chief had authority to direct their activities and operations. The volunteer companies, in an effort to remove themselves from the control of the county, refused to submit to the county's budgetary procedures. The court held that the county, pursuant to the police power, could reasonably regulate the volunteer companies to protect the public health and safety. This meant that the fire chief was clearly in control of direct operations at the scene of any fire and that this authority was not contingent upon a volunteer company's decision to accept public funds. On the other hand, the volunteer companies remained distinct entities and the fire chief could only regulate activities directly related to the fighting of fires. With regard to funding, the court held that if a volunteer company elected to accept county funds, the county could impose conditions on use of those funds. On the other hand, if a volunteer company did not accept county funds, it was only subject to such county regulations as could be imposed under the police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree of the lower court regarding control over volunteer fire companies by the county.

Prince George's County v. Collington Crossroads, Inc.


No. 137, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


275 Md. 171; 339 A.2d 278; 1975 Md. LEXIS 954



June 5, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed July 7, 1975; Denied August 1, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Powers, C. J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County reversed, case remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Costs to be paid by the appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county filed an amended petition against appellee property owner for condemnation of a tract to be used as part of an industrial park. The Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) dismissed the amended petition. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county wanted to exercise its eminent domain authority to condemn a tract for use as part of a proposed industrial park. The property owner objected to the condemnation on the ground that the proposed industrial park was not a public use. The trial court dismissed the case on the ground that the proposed use was a private one. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings because the land sought to be condemned was for a public rather than a private use and therefore the condemnation was permissible under Md. Const. art III, § 40. The court noted that title was not a dispositive criterion and the public benefit had to be measured in order to reach a conclusion. It specifically noted that the county retained important government interests in the industrial park as part of the planned development and that the need had been fully determined by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for further condemnation proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

465 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co. v. Insurance Comm'r


No. 10 (Adv.), September Term, 1975


Court of Appeals of Maryland


275 Md. 130; 339 A.2d 291; 1975 Md. LEXIS 951



June 2, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Liss, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; remanded to the Baltimore City Court with directions to vacate the order of the Insurance Commissioner of Maryland dated January 21, 1975; appellee, Insurance Commissioner, to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer appealed a decision of the City Court of Baltimore (Maryland) that affirmed appellee insurance commissioner's order requiring appellant to renew appellee doctor's insurance policy and accept applications for new policies. Appellant claimed that 1974 Md. Laws 234A, the statute on which the decision was based, did not apply because appellant's actions did not discriminate against a particular class of people.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer petitioned for review of a decision by appellee insurance commissioner that required appellant to renew appellee doctor's malpractice insurance policy and accept applications for new malpractice policies. Appellant claimed that it had to withdraw from the malpractice insurance business because appellee commissioner did not allow it to increase its premiums enough to operate at a profit. Appellee commissioner held that appellant's refusal to renew appellee doctor's policy or accept applications for new policies was unfairly discriminatory under 1974 Md. Laws 234A. Trial court affirmed. Appellant challenged the ruling. Appellate court reversed, explaining that under law 234A, an insurer could not cancel or refuse to underwrite a policy for a particular risk or class of risk for any reason based on race, color, creed, or gender, or for any unfairly discriminatory reason. Appellate court held that under the statute, "risk" meant a person or applicant, not a particular type of insurance. Because the statute was intended to prevent discrimination against particular classes of people, not particular types of insurance policies, it did not apply to appellant's actions.


OUTCOME: Appellate court reversed and remanded trial court's decision affirming an order by appellee insurance commissioner that required appellant insurer to renew appellee doctor's malpractice insurance policy and accept applications for new malpractice policies. The court held that the statute on which the prior decisions were based did not apply because appellant's actions discriminated against a type of insurance, not a class of people.

 

466 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Dimery v. State


No. 161, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


274 Md. 661; 338 A.2d 56; 1975 Md. LEXIS 1235



May 8, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed June 5, 1975; Denied June 24, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, McCullough, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of rape, attempted murder, assault and battery, and arson, and sentenced to life imprisonment. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the conviction and the sentence. Defendant filed a petition for a writ of certiorari and argued that the trial court erroneously failed to instruct the jury that it could limit his sentence on his rape conviction by rendering a verdict without capital punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment for rape, concurrent terms of 20 years each for arson and attempted murder, and a concurrent term of one year for assault and battery. The court granted defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari and affirmed the convictions. The court held that the trial court could impose a sentence of life imprisonment on the rape conviction even though it had failed to instruct the jury that it could limit the sentence by rendering a verdict without capital punishment. The court concluded that defendant had a constitutional right to have the jury instructed as to their statutory right to return a qualified verdict, but that he could waive or forfeit that right by failing to make a timely objection to the instructions. The court did not know why defense counsel did not request an instruction as to the jury's right to limit the period of incarceration by adding the words "without capital punishment." It may have been a matter of trial tactics. However, whatever plain error material to the rights of the accused might have included, it did not include bad guesses by counsel whether or not to object to anything done or left undone by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for rape and his sentence to life imprisonment.

 

467 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Aero Motors, Inc. v. Administrator, Motor Vehicle Administration


No. 105, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


274 Md. 567; 337 A.2d 685; 1975 Md. LEXIS 1228



May 6, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; MacDaniel, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant used car dealers sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) that favored appellees, a state motor vehicle administration and automobile trade association, and declared Md. Ann. Code art. 66 1/2, § 3-113-1, to be constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant used car dealers sought a decree declaring Md. Ann. Code art. 66 1/2, § 3-113.1, unconstitutional and enjoining defendants, a state motor vehicle administration and automobile trade association, from enforcing the statute. Appellants complained that § 3-113.1 violated the equal protection and due process clause of the U.S. Const. amend XIV. Appellants claimed that § 3-113.1 unreasonably required them in the purchase of a new motor vehicle to obtain a certificate of title and that such a transaction was subject to the certificate of title fee and the imposition of an excise tax. These requirements were not imposed upon new car dealers holding franchises from manufacturers and who transferred new vehicles to other dealers having a franchise from the same manufacturer. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the classification made by the legislature was reasonable for the protection of the consumer to insure financial responsibility between the purchasers of a manufacturer's new vehicle and new car dealers, and to guarantee to such purchasers a fulfillment of the manufacturer's warranty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in upholding the constitutionality of the statute because the difference in treatment between appellant used car dealers and new car dealers was reasonable and justified for the protection of consumers.

State's Attorney of Baltimore City v. Baltimore


No. 128, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


274 Md. 597; 337 A.2d 92; 1975 Md. LEXIS 1229



May 6, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Cole, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Paragraphs 3 and 4 of the order of the Superior Court of Baltimore City are deleted, and the order, as so modified, is affirmed. Costs to be evenly divided among the parties.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state's attorney, company, and individual, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which found for appellee city council in a constitutional challenge of Md. Ann. Code art. 53, § 44, and violations of Baltimore, Md., City Ordinance No. 902.


OVERVIEW: At issue was a statute that provided that the responsibility for legal action in cases involving the Building and Electrical Code would be transferred to the city. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment as modified and found that the enactment of the statute violated a restriction upon the authority of the General Assembly imposed by Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 4. The court held that Md. Ann. Code art. 53, § 44 was clearly a public local law. The court also found that mandating that the state's attorney prosecute all violations of the Building and Electrical Codes was an interference by the judiciary with the discretion vested in the state's attorney. Consequently, the portions of the order requiring the state's attorney to prosecute all violations of the Baltimore City Building and Electrical Codes were ordered deleted.


OUTCOME: A judgment of the lower court finding for the city council and against appellants in a constitutional challenge of a statute was affirmed as modified.

 

469 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Everhart v. State


No. 44, September Term, 1974


Court of Appeals of Maryland


274 Md. 459; 337 A.2d 100; 1975 Md. LEXIS 1222



April 14, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland. Circuit Court for Frederick County, Barrick, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; case remanded to that court with directions to reverse the judgments of the Circuit Court for Frederick County and remand the case for a new trial; costs to be paid by Frederick County, Maryland.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions by the circuit court for maintaining a common nuisance and possession of a controlled substance. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed defendant's convictions. Certiorari to the court was granted.


OVERVIEW: At trial, defendant filed a motion to suppress the property seized under the search warrant, alleging that probable cause had not been established and the warrant was issued based upon illegally obtained information. He claimed that tainted evidence obtained from a prior illegal search and seizure conducted at his residence could not be used as the basis to form probable cause in the application for a subsequent warrant. The State argued that only the testimony contained within the "four corners" of the affidavit in the application could be considered. Defendant's motion was denied, and he was subsequently convicted by a jury. On appeal, the court held that (1) the "taint" issue was properly preserved for appellate review, (2) the issuing judge erroneously limited his review to the "four corners" of the affidavit in the application for the search warrant because defendant factually asserted that the evidence was derived from information obtained in an unlawful search and seizure, and (3) defendant was entitled to an evidentiary hearing to determine whether the information relied upon to establish probable cause was illegally obtained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court, and the case was remanded with directions to reverse the judgments of the trial court. A new trial was ordered.
