Maryland Bd. of Pharmacy v. Sav-A-Lot, Inc.


No. 2, September Term, 1973


Court of Appeals of Maryland


270 Md. 103; 311 A.2d 242; 1973 Md. LEXIS 668



October 31, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Carter, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; appellant to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Maryland Board of Pharmacy (board) appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which declared Md. Code Ann. art. 43, § 266A(c)(4)(iv) (1971) unconstitutional as a violation of the due process rights of appellees, corporations which operated retail stores containing pharmacies.


OVERVIEW: The corporations brought a constitutional challenge to § 266A(c)(4)(iv), which prohibited the corporations from advertising prescription drug prices or price discounts on such drugs. The trial court declared the statute unconstitutional under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. On appeal the board argued that the statute was a reasonable exercise of the state's police power. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) the statute could not be constitutionally sanctioned as an exercise of the state's police power because it prohibited advertising of consumer goods sold within the scope of the pharmacist's retail activity and it bore no relation to the wholly permissible regulation of professional services affecting the public health and welfare and (2) the statute was an unconstitutional exercise of the police power because it was in the best interest of the public to be informed of prescription drug prices to enable purchasing at the lowest available prices and there was no substantial relationship between the objectives attributed to the statute and the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order declaring the statute unconstitutional.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction company challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which ruled in favor of appellees, a mayor and a city council, in the construction company's action attacking an ordinance requiring property owners to maintain dwellings in urban renewal areas in accordance with standards not required of all property owners in Baltimore City.

The construction company's bald assertion, without more detail, that there were similar properties in the city not affected by the ordinance simply was not sufficient to overcome the presumption of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree of the trial court, with the construction company to pay the costs.

In re Miles

Court of Appeals of Maryland

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed consolidated appeals on decisions from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City, Division of Juvenile Causes (Maryland), which convicted them of robbery and burglary. Defendants asserted that their waiver hearing did not occur until they were 21, and therefore they should have been released.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were under the age of 16 when they committed the offense for which they were convicted. However, they were not given a waiver hearing under after they were 21. They were thereafter convicted of robbery and burglary. Defendant asserted that they should have been released because the trial court lacked jurisdiction over them as they were not sent to the trial court by the juvenile court as statutorily required. the court vacated their convictions and remanded for further proceedings, holding that if the chancellor concluded that a waiver should have been ordered in any one or more of the four cases the named defendants could be tried de novo in the trial court. In any case in which the chancellor concluded that a waiver should have been refused the named defendants should have been released, unless, of course, they were being legally detained for other reasons.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendants' convictions and remanded the cases for further hearings and determinations.

Hearst Corp. (News American Div.) v. State Dep't of Assessments & Taxation


No. 342, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 625; 308 A.2d 679; 1973 Md. LEXIS 855



August 17, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Maryland Tax Court; Korn, C. J., and Blair and Hughes, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Order of 1 November 1972 reversed; case remanded for entry of an order conformable to the views expressed in this opinion; costs to be paid by appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper corporation challenged an order of the Maryland Tax Court, which upheld an assessment by appellee, the State Department Of Assessments. The Department entered a cross-appeal of that part of the order that held that 11 day's of newsprint were tax-exempt.


OVERVIEW: The Department denied the newspaper's request for an exemption of its entire newsprint because is was a raw material used in manufacturing. The tax court affirmed the assessments, but allowed 11 days' of newsprint as an exemption. On appeal, the newspaper based its claim on long-standing case law that held that the printing of newspapers was not "manufacturing" for tax purposes. Also, the Department cross-appealed, contending that the entire inventory of newsprint was taxable. The court held that, 1) the newspaper's mechanical operations constituted manufacturing; 2) its tools and machinery used in the manufacturing were exempt under Baltimore, Md., Code art. 28, § 83(a) (1966); and its inventory of raw materials was also exempt. The court noted that although tax-exemption statutes were strictly construed, and prior case law exempted the industry altogether, much had changed in both the newspaper business and the local laws. The court also stated that doctrine of stare decisis did not prevent the court from changing a rule of law laid down in prior case law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the tax court and remanded for further proceedings.

Chillum--Adelphi Volunteer Fire Dep't v. Prince George's County


No. 324, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 486; 307 A.2d 481; 1973 Md. LEXIS 845



July 9, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; McCullough, J.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded without affirmance or reversal pursuant to Rule 871 a for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion, the costs to be paid by the appellee and cross-appellant, Prince George's County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Volunteer Fire Departments, and appellee, Prince George's County, challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which declared that the legal and beneficial interest in the assets of the Volunteer Fire Departments was in the respective volunteer fire companies and that the assets were not held by those companies upon any express, implied, or charitable trust for the County.


OVERVIEW: The declaratory relief sought concerned the legality, construction, and effect of various provisions of the Code of Public Local Laws of Prince George's County, Resolutions of the Board of County Commissioners for Prince George's County, and provisions of the Prince George's County Charter as they related to appellants. Appellants successfully contended at trial that the entire application of Prince George's County, Md., Code Pub. Loc. Laws § 32-17 was limited by subsection (e) to volunteer fire companies and rescue squads so that the provisions of subsection (c) in regard to assets did not apply to them. The court stated that by limiting the application of the statute to volunteer fire companies and rescue squads organized after the effective date of the statute, it was unnecessary for the trial court to decide the constitutional issues inevitably arising if the statute was construed in the manner urged by the County. The court stated that it was the legislative intent of § 32-17 to apply subsections (a), (b), (c) and (d) to the volunteer fire companies and rescue squads existing when the Act became effective; therefore, the constitutional issues raised had to be decided.


OUTCOME: The court remanded without affirmance or reversal so that the trial court could have taken additional testimony and decide and declare whether or not, and to what extent the statutory provisions were unconstitutional.

Washington County Taxpayers Asso. v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 328, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 454; 306 A.2d 539; 1973 Md. LEXIS 842



July 6, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Washington County; Rutledge, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree modified and as modified affirmed; appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, who were taxpayers and a taxpayers association, sought review of an adverse judgment by the Circuit Court for Washington County (Maryland) in their action against appellee county to obtain a declaratory judgment that the county's land use plan was invalid, unconstitutional, and unenforceable. The action also sought an injunction against administering, enforcing, or applying the plan's provisions to appellants or to their property.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged the county's comprehensive land use plan on the ground that the notice of a public hearing to consider the plan was not legally adequate and that the hearing did not afford the public the opportunity to speak against the plan and to oppose the concept of and the need for it. The court modified the circuit court's judgment in favor of the county by adding a statement that the plan was validly adopted and affirmed the judgment as modified. In its ruling, the court found that the notice that the county issued informed the citizenry that a public hearing would be held in connection with the proposed plan. That was notice that was calculated to inform any interested citizens of the need to attend the hearing if they desired to inform themselves or to express their views concerning the plan. The evidence showed that those present at the hearing were permitted the opportunity and sufficient time to express their general opposition to the plan's adoption. The court held that the three-minute limitation on speakers, when coupled with the county's offer to accept the written statements of any participant, did not impair the validity of the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by adding language to the effect that the adoption of the county's plan was valid and affirmed the judgment as modified.

 

511 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Anne Arundel County v. Moushabek


No. 84 (Adv.), September Term, 1973


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 419; 306 A.2d 517; 1973 Md. LEXIS 838



July 5, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Wray, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree modified and as modified affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a decree from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which was entered in favor of appellee property owners in a zoning dispute.


OVERVIEW: The county city council adopted a comprehensive zoning ordinance for the northern portion of the third assessment district of the county. On appeal, the court sought to determine whether amendments to the county zoning ordinance were properly adopted and, if not, whether their invalidity vitiated the entire zoning ordinance. The court answered both questions in the negative. There was no contention that the charter provision was anything other than mandatory if the amendments were found to have been amendments "of substance." It was obvious that council and executive regarded the amendments as severable from the main body of the ordinance. Otherwise, the executive would not have vetoed some of the amendments and the council would not have sustained the veto to part, but not all, of those amendments. Had there been no amendments, the ordinance would have been complete as a vehicle for determining the permitted land uses in the district. The court determined that the invalid provisions of the ordinance could have been eliminated and the legislative intention easily carried out. Accordingly, the chancellor erred in not determining that the ordinance was severable.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's decree to the extent that the declaratory decree should have spelled out the valid adoption of the ordinance, but specified that the amendments were invalidly adopted and hence ineffective, and as modified affirmed.

Ballard v. Supervisor of Assessments


No. 330, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 397; 306 A.2d 506; 1973 Md. LEXIS 835



July 5, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Maryland Tax Court; Korn, C. J., and Logan, Blair, Hughes and Arthur, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Maryland Tax Court affirmed; appellants to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the decision from the Maryland Tax Court, which affirmed respondent assessor's denial of the taxpayers' application for an exemption from property tax assessment on the ground that their residence and taxpayer husband's place of business was used as a place of worship for his congregation.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers applied for a property tax exemption for property used as a family home, the taxpayer husband's place of business, and a place of worship for his congregation. The assessor denied the application. His assessment was affirmed by the tax court because of the nonexempt activities conducted on the premises. The taxpayers claimed that the refusal to give them the exemption granted to other churches, many of which engaged in secular activities, violated Md. Const. Decl. Rts. arts. 15, 36, and the First and Fourteenth Amendments. On appeal the court affirmed the tax court's decision. The court held that: (1) the taxpayer's property was neither a house used exclusively for public worship or a parsonage used in connection therewith, where it was used regularly three to four hours each day for commercial purposes and used as the taxpayers' residence in addition to the thrice-weekly services attended by the public; (2) although the property was used to produce income to support a public worship use, it was not thereby made exempt; and (3) the tax court's application of the exemption did not violate state or federal constitutional law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's decision, which upheld the assessor's denial of the taxpayers' application for exemption from property tax where the taxpayers' residence was used for commercial purposes and as a residence in addition to public worship.

 

513 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Director, Patuxent Institution v. Cash


Nos. 287, 318, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 331; 305 A.2d 833; 1973 Md. LEXIS 828



June 14, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] In No. 287, appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Shearin, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.

In No. 318, appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County; Macgill, C. J.



DISPOSITION: Order of October 4, 1972, in No. 287 reversed, and decree of January 10, 1973, in No. 318 affirmed. The costs to be paid by the appellant in No. 287 and by the appellee in No. 318.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which granted petitioner inmates' application for writs of habeas corpus requiring their release from respondent mental institution to correctional facilities because the institution failed to timely evaluate the inmates and file reports as required by Md. Ann. Code art. 31B, § 7(a).


OVERVIEW: The inmates, who had been convicted of various crimes, were sent to the mental institution for evaluation as defective delinquents. Staff at the mental institution was unable to evaluate the inmates because the inmates refused to cooperate. In the first action, the inmates sought their release to correctional facilities because the mental institution failed to evaluate them and make reports to the court within six months, as required by art. 31B, § 7(a). In a second case, the state sought and was granted a declaratory judgment, that the reporting provision of the statute was not mandatory where the inmates refused to cooperate. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment that granted the inmates' writs of habeas corpus and affirmed the judgment that declared the reporting provision directory. The court reasoned that, although the provision appeared to be mandatory, it was directory in cases where the inmate refused to cooperate since making it mandatory would have resulted in the release of uncooperative inmates due to delays that they had caused. The court noted that there was no penalty for the mental institution's failure to timely file reports under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that granted the inmates' petitions for writs of habeas corpus that required their release from the mental institution. The court affirmed the judgment that declared that the statutory requirement that the mental institution make an evaluation of the inmates and file a report with the court within six months was directory where the inmates failed to cooperate with evaluation.

Andresen v. Bar Asso. of Montgomery County


No. 336, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland

DISPOSITION: Order of December 19, 1972, modified in accordance with the views expressed in this opinion and as modified affirmed; costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Montgomery County, which granted a petition filed by appellee county bar association pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 21, § 7-106 (1973), and ordered an audit of the attorney's accounts for funds received in connection with real estate closing transactions in the State of Maryland.


OVERVIEW: Following criminal charges being filed against the attorney in a separate case, the county bar association filed a petition in the trial court in accordance with Md. Ann. Code art. 21, § 7-106 (1973) for an audit of the attorney's accounts for funds received in connection with real estate closing transactions in the State of Maryland. The trial court ordered the audit. On review, the court modified the order of the trial court and affirmed the order as modified. The court modified the trial court's order, however, to limit the audit to the time period following November 2, 1970. Moreover, the court modified the trial court's order to limit the audit, in its initial phase, to the real estate transactions in question. The court held that, if warranted, the scope of the audit could be expanded to include other real estate transactions.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the trial court and affirmed the order as modified.

 

515 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Reeder v. Board of Supervisors


No. 286, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 261; 305 A.2d 132; 1973 Md. LEXIS 822



June 6, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County; Wise, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, the appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident sought review from the decision of the Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County (Maryland), which sustained the demurrer of appellee elections board in the resident's action appealing the board's refusal to register the resident to vote in Queen Anne County on local issues and offices only.


OVERVIEW: The resident owned and lived in two houses, one in Baltimore City and one in Queen Anne's County. The resident was domiciled in Baltimore City. The resident claimed that because he was forced to pay taxes for his house in Queen Anne's County, the refusal to allow him to vote on local issues was a violation of Md. Const. art. I, § 1. The court affirmed and held that contrary to the resident's claim, county elections were not excluded from the scope of Md. Ann. Code art. 33, § 1-1(a)(6) (1971) because they were clearly intended to be included within the statutes dealing with elections; thus the resident was granted his right by being able to vote in one election. The court also held that the resident was not denied any rights under U.S. Const. amend. 14, § 1 because states were allowed to impose bona fide vote qualification, and restricting voters to those who held domicile in the locality was within the state's power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Prince George's County v. Maryland--National Capital Park & Planning Com.


No. 269, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


269 Md. 202; 306 A.2d 223; 1973 Md. LEXIS 818



June 5, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing and Modification Filed June 21, 1973; Denied July 2, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowen, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree of October 2, 1972, affirmed, the appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), holding that appellee Maryland-National Capital Park and Planning Commission (commission) had standing to sue, that there were justiciable issues ripe for declaratory decree, and that the Regional District Act (Act), Md. Laws ch. 780 (1959), was a public general law and not subject to amendment or superceding by county charter.


OVERVIEW: The General Assembly created the commission and it was given the duties to administer certain park development, planing, and zoning functions within portions of two counties, the Maryland-Washington Metropolitan District. Later laws created the Maryland-Washington Regional District, which included the first district along with other areas. The commission's park and planning functions were separated, repealed, and then consolidated in the Act. On appeal, the court ruled that the commission had standing to maintain the suit for declaratory relief under § 11 of the Act. Declaratory relief was proper when two agencies were in dispute. There were a number of issues that were ripe for declaratory relief. There were issues over the levying of taxes, the propriety of legislative activities on behalf of the committee, the transfer of employees between the parties, and the commission's power to acquire land, to name a few. The court also found that the Act was a public general law because it concerned several geographic subdivisions of the state and the titles indicated that they were enacted as bi-county acts. Thus, the county charter could not amend or supercede the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the commission had standing to sue, that there were ripe issues to be decided by declaratory decree, and that the Act was not a public local law, but rather a public general law.

In re Diener


Misc. (Judicial Disabilities) No. 1, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


268 Md. 659; 304 A.2d 587; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1139



May 11, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration and Clarification Filed by A. Jerome Diener May 25, 1973; Amended Order Filed June 6, 1973. Motion for Rehearing Filed by Joseph L. Broccolino June 6, 1973; Denied June 11, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Findings, Conclusions and Recommendations of the Commission on Judicial Disabilities.



DISPOSITION: Order entered that Judge A. Jerome Diener and Judge Joseph L. Broccolino, Jr., be, and they are hereby, removed as Judges of the District Court of Maryland.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commission on Judicial Disabilities recommended censure of respondent judges, who had engaged in conduct prejudicial to the proper administration of justice while serving as judges of the Traffic Division of the Municipal Court of Baltimore City. Both judges filed motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Commission on Judicial Disabilities (commission) investigated the judges and found that, while there was no evidence of the judges' personal financial gain, they did dispose of parking ticket cases, reach verdicts of either not guilty, or did suspend and reduce fines for reasons of friendship, political favoritism, or the importuning of court clerks. The commission determined that the judges had engaged in conduct prejudicial to the proper administration of justice and recommended their censure. Both judges filed motions to dismiss. The court accepted the commission's findings of fact and denied the judges' motions to dismiss. The court held that the commission's findings were supported by clear and convincing evidence and that the aim of the commission's proceedings was the maintenance of the honor and dignity of the judiciary and the proper administration of justice rather than punishment. The court found that the judges' lack of financial benefit from their actions was irrelevant and that justice demanded their removal sanctioned by Md. Const. art. IV, § 4B.


OUTCOME: The court accepted the findings of fact of the Commission on Judicial Disabilities and ordered the removal of the judges without the prejudice to their pensions or other employment benefits.

Prince George's County v. McBride


No. 203, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


268 Md. 522; 302 A.2d 620; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1126



April 4, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Loveless, J.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant District Council sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which declared 1969 Md. Laws 278 unconstitutional and ordered that the Council grant appellee property owner's application for reclassification of his land in the property owner's appeal from the Council's denial of his reclassification application.


OVERVIEW: The property owner filed an application with the Council for reclassification of his land from local commercial to light industrial. The Council referred the matter to the municipality in which the land was located for its recommendation pursuant to Prince George's County, Md., Code Pub. Loc. Laws § 59-83(c) (1966). The municipality recommended denial of the application. The Council denied the application for want of a two-thirds majority vote as required by 1969 Md. Laws 278. Upon judicial review, the trial court declared 1969 Md. Laws 278 unconstitutional for the reason that it delegated zoning power to municipalities without providing necessary standards. The trial court ordered the Council to approve the application. Upon further review, the court reversed the trial court's order, holding that 1969 Md. Laws 278 was not unconstitutional. The court found that 1969 Md. Laws 278 did not have the effect of delegating zoning power to municipalities. The court determined that the trial court should have upheld the Council's denial of the owner's reclassification application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded for an order declaring the statute constitutional and an order affirming the Council's denial of the owner's application for reclassification.

Dryfoos v. Hostetter


No. 210, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


268 Md. 396; 302 A.2d 28; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1114



March 27, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed April 26, 1973; Denied May 7, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowie, J.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, case remanded for the entry of a decree conformable to the views expressed in this opinion. Costs below and on appeal to be paid by Suburban Home Investment Corporation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant buyers sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which held that the first trust was valid and that the second trust subordinated to it by a subordination agreement. Plaintiff sellers challenged the order granting validity and priority to the first trust.


OVERVIEW: The buyers and sellers entered into an agreement to for the purchase of a parcel of property. The sellers subsequently sold the same piece of property to another individual. The property was encumbered by a loan proceeds from both two trusts. The second purchaser secured the first trust, and the buyers secured the second trust. The buyers defaulted. The sellers filed a suit to enjoin the second trust from foreclosing. The first trust filed a third-party claim and alleged that it had the first secured lien. The trial court agreed with the first trust and held that the first trust had the first secured lien. The buyers and sellers sought review. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held: (1) there was no affidavit of disbursement of the deed of trust of the first trust, therefore the deed was void, not only as to third parties, but as between the parties themselves; and (2) the first deed of trust had no effect, and during that period the buyers were secured by a senior incumbrance on the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that held that the first trust was valid and that the second trust was subordinated to it. The court held that the first trust was void and had no effect.

Gatewood v. State


No. 195, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


268 Md. 349; 301 A.2d 498; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1109



March 20, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Baltimore City Court; Jones, J.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied; order affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant, Bland R. B. Gatewood.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Baltimore City Court (Maryland), which ordered the forfeiture of a monetary amount found in close proximity to controlled dangerous substances incident to an execution of a valid search warrant. Defendant pled guilty and was convicted of possession of controlled dangerous substances. After the conviction defendant filed a petition for the return of the seized funds.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a valid search warrant, police officers discovered a brown paper bag in defendant's bedroom. The bag contained four bags of heroin, a bottle of marijuana, and a bank money bag containing $ 1,862.10 in cash. Defendant sought to reclaim the money. The money was to be used to pay defendant's attorney. Defendant pled guilty and was convicted of possession of controlled dangerous substances. The trial court ordered that the money be forfeited to the State. On appeal, the court affirmed and rejected defendant's argument that the forfeiture statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297, violated his due process rights and his right to equal protection. The court also rejected defendant's argument that there was no evidence that the money was found in the proximity of the drugs. The court found that the record specifically stated that the money was found in the same bag as the drugs. The court found that the fact that the State failed to institute the forfeiture proceeding until five months after the conviction did not violate any requirement of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the forfeiture order. The court denied the State's motion to dismiss. The court ordered that defendant pay the costs.

Baltimore v. Mano Swartz, Inc.


No. 145, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


268 Md. 79; 299 A.2d 828; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1088; 4 ERC (BNA) 2034; 3 ELR 20232



February 8, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Perrott, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed, costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which found that a city ordinance that governed the size and design of signs in the business district was invalid. The trial court permanently restrained the city from requiring the removal of signs maintained by appellee local businesses.


OVERVIEW: The local businesses challenged the ordinance claiming that it in no way promoted the public health, safety, security, or morals of the community, and was not a proper exercise of the city's police power. The city maintained that the ordinance was a valid use of police power under its charter. The trial court found that the ordinance was based upon aesthetic considerations alone, which was an invalid use of the city's police power. Upon review, the court affirmed. It found that the sole purpose of the ordinance was to achieve an aesthetically pleasing result with no thought to enhancing public welfare. Thus, it was invalid. The court observed that if the ordinance had attempted to preserve or protect something aesthetically pleasing, that might have been a valid use of the city's police power. Further, the court found that because the ordinance was an amendment to a zoning law, it was enacted without complying with the substantive and procedural requirements of the Zoning Enabling Act, Md. Code art. 66B (1957). The city derived its zoning power from the act, and not its charter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the city ordinance that governed the size and design of signs in the business district was invalid.

Salisbury Beauty Schools v. State Board of Cosmetologists


No. 78, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


268 Md. 32; 300 A.2d 367; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1086



February 7, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court No. 2 of Baltimore City; Cardin, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed, the costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beauty schools filed suit seeking a declaration that Md. Ann. Code art. 43, § 537 (1971), was unconstitutional and an injunction against enforcement by appellee state board of cosmetology (board). The Circuit Court No. 2 of Baltimore City (Maryland) granted summary judgment for the board and the beauty schools appealed.


OVERVIEW: The beauty schools protested the board's admonishment to lower their clinic prices in accordance with Md. Ann. Code art. 43, § 537(a) (1971), arguing that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court declared that the statute was constitutional and referred the issue of a price schedule to the board for promulgation of rules and regulations. On appeal, the court held that (1) the beauty schools could not argue that genuine disputes of material facts existed because at the trial level, they stipulated that no such issues existed, (2) the state possessed the police power to protect and promote the public health and safety of its citizenry and the statutory limitation on charges by the beauty schools restricted them to the primary function for which they were licensed, which was the training of students, (3) § 537(a) had a substantial direct relationship with the health, safety, and welfare of the public and did not violate equal protection, and (4) the fact that the board had historically chosen not to enforce the statute did not subject the state to the application of either equitable estoppel or laches.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for the board.

Mass Transit Administration v. Baltimore County Revenue Authority


No. 143, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 687; 298 A.2d 413; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1284



January 11, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; MacDaniel, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Mass Transit Administration (MTA) challenged a decree of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) that declared the MTA responsible for the payment of tolls charged by appellee Baltimore County Revenue Authority for the use by the MTA buses of two bridges owned by the Revenue Authority.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to a decree of the circuit court declaring that the MTA was required to pay the tolls charged by the Revenue Authority for the use by the MTA buses of two bridges owned by the Revenue Authority, the MTA appealed arguing that it was performing a governmental function and a public purpose and should have been included within the ambit of the exemption provided by § 502 of the Trust Indenture. The Trust Indenture was entered into pursuant to the authority of the Revenue Authority. In the alternative the MTA maintained that Md. Code art. 64B exempted it from the payment of the tolls. Affirming the circuit court's judgment, the court held that the exemption under the Trust Indenture was not a broad governmental exemption, but rather an exemption limited to specific Baltimore County officials and official vehicles, and official vehicles of the State Police of Maryland. With respect to art. 64B, the court determined that its title, which was relevant to ascertainment of its intent and purpose, was for a "tax exemption," and tolls were clearly neither taxes nor charges in the nature of taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which required the MTA to pay tolls for the use of two bridges by the MTA buses.

Administrator, Motor Vehicle Administration v. Vogt


No. 118, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 660; 299 A.2d 1; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1282



January 11, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed February 13, 1973; Denied February 26, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Carroll County; Weant, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; judgment entered declaring article 66 1/2, § 203 (d) to be constitutional; cross-appeal dismissed; appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Administrator of the Motor Vehicles Administration, challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland), which entered an injunction in favor of appellees, automobile wreckers. The trial court held that Md. Ann. Code art. 66 1/2, § 5-203(d) (Repl. Vol. 1970) was unconstitutional on the ground that it violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The wreckers brought an action at law for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief on the ground that an assessment was unconstitutionally imposed upon wreckers and not upon scrap processors. The Administrator argued that a $ 5.00 assessment imposed by Md. Ann. Code art. 66 1/2, § 5-203(d) (Repl. Vol. 1970), statute did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. Specifically, he claimed that the distinction made between wreckers and scrap processors had a reasonable relation to the legislative purpose underlying the statute. First the court dismissed the wrecker's cross-appeal because they were deemed the prevailing party in the lower proceedings. Further, the court held that the wreckers failed in their burden of proving that the statute violated a constitutional right. The court determined that the differences in classification and treatment was related to reducing the extensive storage of old automobile hulks, which in turn, reduced ecological damage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and entered a judgment declaring the statute constitutional. The wreckers' cross-appeal was dismissed.

 

525 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Small v. Secretary of Personnel


No. 135, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 532; 298 A.2d 173; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1269



January 3, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed February 2, 1973; Denied February 5, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Harris, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which denied his petition for a writ of mandamus to obtain an order directing appellee Secretary of Personnel of the State of Maryland to hold an administrative hearing on the employee's termination from state service.


OVERVIEW: The employee was given a temporary appointment to state service and was advised that permanent appointments were made through selection from eligible lists established as a result of merit system examinations. After he took his examination but before the eligible list was published, the employee was notified that his employment was being terminated. The employee sought a writ of mandamus to compel the Secretary to hold an administrative hearing. He claimed that he was entitled to a hearing because his probationary period began with his temporary appointment and that he had completed his probationary period at the time he successfully passed the examination and was placed on the eligible list for permanent employment. The trial court denied his petition and the court affirmed. It found that the employee's appointment was a temporary one, pending establishment of an eligible list for permanent employment. Further, unless and until the employee was given a permanent appointment, his probationary period did not begin to run. Accordingly, at the time of his discharge, the employee was a temporary employee and could be removed without a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied the employee's petition for writ of mandamus seeking an order directing the Secretary to hold an administrative hearing on the employee's termination from state service.

 

526 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Giant of Maryland, Inc. v. State's Attorney for Prince George's County


Nos. 116, 149, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 501; 298 A.2d 427; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1265



January 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] In No. 116, appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Taylor, J.

In No. 149, two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Taylor, J.



DISPOSITION: As to appeal No. 116: Cease and desist order dated June 20, 1972 vacated; case remanded for entry of a decree enjoining Giant of Maryland, Inc. from violating Article 27, § 534H in accordance with the views expressed in this opinion. Costs to be paid by appellant. As to appeal No. 149: Orders dated June 20, 1972 dismissing petitions for injunctive relief vacated; case remanded for the entry of decrees enjoining The Grand Union Company and Safeway Stores, Incorporated from violating Article 27, § 534H in accordance with the views expressed in this opinion. Costs to be paid 1/2 by each appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant grocery chain appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which ordered it to cease and desist operating with more than six employees at a given time in any one store with respect to Sunday operations. Plaintiff state's attorney appealed orders of the trial court that dismissed his petition to enjoin defendants, two other grocery chains, from operating on Sunday.


OVERVIEW: The state's attorney filed petitions to enjoin three grocery chains from violating Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 534H (1957, 1971 Repl. Vol.), a "Sunday Blue Law." The trial court enjoined the first chain from conducting business on Sunday with more than six employees at any given time in any store. The trial court dismissed the petitions against the other two chains. On appeal, the court vacated the trial court's orders and remanded for entry of decrees enjoining the chains from violating § 534H. The court held that the small business exception in § 534H(c)3 did not exempt from regulation any business that, on Sunday, operated with not more than six employees on any one shift at any one location. Nothing in § 534H suggested that "any one shift" meant "any one shift on Sunday." Only those businesses that regularly operated with not more than six employees on any shift could lawfully do business on Sunday in the county. None of the chains qualified for the small business exemption. Section 534H was sufficiently explicit to enable a person of ordinary intelligence to ascertain with a fair degree of precision what it prohibited and what conduct would render him liable to its penalties.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the cease and desist order that was entered in the first case and remanded the case for entry of a decree enjoining the grocery chain from violating the "Sunday Blue Law." The court vacated the orders dismissing petitions for injunctive relief in the other cases and remanded the cases for entry of decrees enjoining the other grocery chains from violating the "Sunday Blue Law."

Prince George's County v. One (1) 1969 Opel


No. 101, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 491; 298 A.2d 168; 1973 Md. LEXIS 1264



January 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; McCullough, J.



DISPOSITION: Orders of 2 March and 3 March 1972 reversed. Cases remanded for further proceedings. Costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which determined the forfeiture statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297 (1971 Repl. Vol.), was unconstitutional and ordered the return of the vehicles to appellees.


OVERVIEW: Two vehicles belonging to appellees were forfeited pursuant to the forfeiture statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297 (1971 Repl. Vol.). The purpose of the forfeiture statute was to deter the violations of narcotics laws through the use of a vehicle. Nonetheless, the trial court declared that § 297 was unconstitutional and ordered the return of the vehicles to appellees. The trial court found that the rules laid down in § 297 were hopelessly standardless because they did not provide any guidance as to the terms and conditions for the forfeiture of an automobile. The county filed an appeal. The court held that the lack of complicity by appellees, unless rescued by a stated exception, was not a defense and in fact made no difference whether there was any conviction of a crime related to the seized vehicles. The court agreed that the forfeiture statute, as provided in § 297, was a harsh law. However, the court noted that it was within the legislature's power to decide that such harshness was required for deterring the proliferation of drugs. The court reversed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that determined that the forfeiture statute was unconstitutional and ordered the return of the vehicles to appellees. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

528 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Montgomery County


No. 95, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 456; 298 A.2d 178; 1972 Md. LEXIS 684



December 22, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Mathias, Joseph M., J.



DISPOSITION: Order of April 27, 1972, affirmed, the appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which granted summary judgment to defendants, county, trustees of the county community college, and the state Board of Public Works (trustees), on the owners' request for an injunction against expenditure of funds for the expansion of a college campus.


OVERVIEW: The principal questions presented for review involved the alleged unconstitutionality of Md. Ann. Code art. 77A, §§ 1-10 (1957, 1969 Repl. Vol.), particularly § 1 (d), giving the trustees power to purchase, lease, condemn or in any other manner acquire real and personal property deemed necessary by them for the operation of the community college. The court held that the state could delegate its power of eminent domain to a school and that no guides or standards needed to be given when the power was so delegated. However, the delegation of power to the trustees was limited by § 1(d) to land deemed necessary for the operation of the community college. The court concluded that the delegation of the power of eminent domain to the trustees was not unconstitutional because of a lack of sufficient guides and standards. The court found that the affidavits in support of the summary judgment motion set forth in substantial detail all of the opportunities to be heard which were given to the property owners, sufficient to satisfy their due process rights. It also found no constitutional violation in using public funds to purchase property from a church for the school's use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to grant summary judgment to the trustees because there was no constitutional violation in delegating the power of eminent domain to them, due process requirements had been met, and public funds could be used to purchase property that belonged to a church when needed for the college.

 

529 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Bartholomey v. State


No. 106, September Term, 1970, No. 386, September Term, 1971, Misc. Nos. 2, 3, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 175; 297 A.2d 696; 1972 Md. LEXIS 664



December 4, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 106, Appeal from the Circuit Court for Charles County; Digges, C. J.

No. 386, Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Mathias, Robert B., J.

Misc. No. 2, Petition to vacate illegal sentence from the Criminal Court of Baltimore; Carter, Joseph L., J.

Misc. No. 3, Petition to vacate illegal sentence from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County; Duer and Travers, JJ.



DISPOSITION: No. 106: Case remanded to the trial court for imposition of life sentences in accordance with the views expressed and procedures outlined in this opinion. No. 386: Sentence of death vacated; case remanded to the trial court for imposition of a life sentence in accordance with the views expressed and procedures outlined in this opinion. No. 2: Appeal dismissed for want of jurisdiction. No. 3: Appeal dismissed for want of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their death sentences entered by the Circuit Courts for Charles, Prince George's, and Wicomico Counties, and the Criminal Court of Baltimore (Maryland).


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed the death sentences imposed on various defendants in light of a United States Supreme Court decision holding that discretionary death sentences were unconstitutional. Three of the defendants were convicted of murder and sentenced to death. A fourth defendant was convicted of rape and sentenced to death. As to the defendants convicted of murder, the court vacated defendants' sentences and remanded to the trial court for resentencing. The court noted that the invalidity of the death sentences did not affect the legality of the underlying murder convictions. The court further held that the only sentence that could be imposed was for life imprisonment pursuant to Md. Code of 1957 art. 27, § 413. As to the defendant convicted of rape, his sentence was also vacated, but the court noted that a defendant convicted of rape could be sentenced to life imprisonment under Md. Code of 1957 art. 27, § 416, or to a lesser sentence of from 18 months to 21 years. As to all defendants, the court noted that the sentencing judges could inquire into the past criminal record of the defendants and hear evidence and receive reports in aggravation or mitigation of punishment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentences of defendants and ordered that they be resentenced.

State v. McCray


No. 45, September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


267 Md. 111; 297 A.2d 265; 1972 Md. LEXIS 662

DISPOSITION: Order of 24 February 1972 reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mentally ill inmates challenged decisions of the Circuit Courts for Howard and Montgomery Counties (Maryland), which adopted rules to purportedly dispel all constitutional deficiencies in civil commitment cases in appellee State and then retained jurisdiction over the complaints.


OVERVIEW: Sentenced under the Defective Delinquent Act, Md. Ann. Code art. 31b, § 5, mentally ill inmates challenged their civil commitment by filing applications for writs of habeas corpus and petitions for injunctive relief, alleging violations of their constitutional rights under the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments. On appeal, the court sua sponte determined that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the cause. However, the court did determine that the inmates could proceed under the Inmate Grievance Commission Act, Md. Ann. Code art. 41, § 204F.


OUTCOME: The court found that it did not have jurisdiction to hear the raised complaints but reversed the decision of the trial court as to the injunctive relief.

 

531 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Potomac Sand & Gravel Co. v. Governor of Maryland


No. 35 (Adv.), September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


266 Md. 358; 293 A.2d 241; 1972 Md. LEXIS 742; 2 ELR 20101



July 6, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Evans, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed, the appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), in favor of defendant Governor of Maryland, in an action for a declaratory judgment in which the property owner requested that 1971 Md. Laws 792; Code of Public Local Laws of Charles County (1969 Ed.), art. 9, § 337A (Chapter 792) be declared to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The property owner was engaged in the business of dredging sand and gravel. It owned three parcels of land, the uses of which were at issue. All three parcels were located in Charles County, Maryland, and all three were adjoined to or surrounded by state wetlands. All three parcels were within the proscription of ch. 792. In issue was whether the legislature by enacting Public Local Law, ch. 792, might absolutely prohibit anyone, including the property owner from dredging, taking and carrying away sand and gravel from the tidal waters or marshlands of Charles County. The court held that ch. 792 was a legitimate exercise of the police power by the legislature to regulate and restrain a particular use, that would be inconsistent with or injurious to the rights of the public, of property within the control of the state. Such regulation and restraint was not an unconstitutional taking of private property for public use without just compensation, as prohibited by the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and Article 23 of the Declaration of Rights of the Constitution of Maryland.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree below and found the statute constitutional.

 

532 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Siegel


No. 8 (Adv.), September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


266 Md. 256; 292 A.2d 86; 1972 Md. LEXIS 734



July 3, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland.



DISPOSITION: Order dismissing indictment affirmed. Costs to be paid by Mayor and City Council of Baltimore City.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state petitioned for a writ of certiorari, seeking review of a decision from the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, which affirmed a trial court's order suppressing all the intercepted conversations of the accused that served as the basis for an indictment charging him with conspiracy to violate the lottery laws of the state. The trial court found that the conversations were unlawfully intercepted in violation of the accused's rights.


OVERVIEW: The accused was indicted for conspiracy to violate the lottery laws of the state, based on the state's interception of the accused's telephone and oral conversations. The accused filed a motion to suppress the electronically acquired evidence and the trial court granted it, dismissing the indictment, and found that the conversations were unlawfully intercepted. The appellate court affirmed the order and the state petitioned for a writ of certiorari, which the court granted. The court thereafter affirmed the order dismissing the indictment, holding that the wiretap orders were void because they failed to meet certain preconditions provided in Title III of the Omnibus Crime Control and Safe Streets Act of 1968, 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 2510-20 (Act), which was designed to protect the accused's constitutional rights and thus, the evidence that arose from them had to be suppressed. The court found that the Act not only complied with the Fourth Amendment, but was also properly implemented under the laws of Maryland, and set up a strict procedure for electronic surveillance that had to be followed, as no deviation from the procedure, no matter how slight, would be tolerated by the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the indictment against the accused charging conspiracy to violate the lottery laws of the state of Maryland, which indictment was based on unlawfully intercepted telephone and oral conversations of the accused.

Weil v. Supervisor of Assessments of Washington County


No. 398, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


266 Md. 238; 292 A.2d 68; 1972 Md. LEXIS 733



July 3, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed July 25, 1972; Denied September 11, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Washington County; Ottinger, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of the decision rendered by the Circuit Court for Washington County (Maryland). The circuit court ruled that the valuation of taxes on the land given by appellee supervisor of assessments was appropriate.


OVERVIEW: The landowners and the supervisor of assessments disagreed as to the value of land improved by gasoline service stations. The landowners presented an expert appraiser and the appraiser contended that the market data approach was the proper method to value the land because he said a market existed, although he used no service station sales for comparable sales on the ground that he found none close enough. The court stated that the fact that one lot was assessed at one figure per square foot and another lot at a different figure per square foot did not show discrimination in the absence of a showing that the two lots were in fact so similar in all respects as to be identical in value. The court also stated that there had not been even the slightest intimation of lack of good faith upon the part of the taxing authorities. Therefore, it could not be said that there had been conscious, arbitrary discrimination against the landowners. The order rendered by the circuit court was affirmed and the landowners were obliged to pay costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court in favor of the supervisor of assessments, in the landowners' action challenging the method of valuation of their land for tax purposes.

Selinger v. Governor of Maryland


No. 100 (Adv.), September Term, 1972


Court of Appeals of Maryland


266 Md. 431; 293 A.2d 817; 1972 Md. LEXIS 748



June 30, 1972  
July 20, 1972, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Childs, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner residents challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which denied their bill for declaratory and injunctive relief against respondent governor seeking a declaration that certain bills were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The General Assembly enacted certain house bills which, provided that under certain circumstances costs of school construction would thereafter be funded by the State. The residents endeavored to have the bills brought to referendum. The bills were passed by the House of Delegates and by the Senate. The bills were presented to the Governor, and signed by him. The residents argued that they were advised that the petitions designed to take a bill to referendum could not be signed until the Governor approved the bill. The Governor signed the bills just prior to a holiday weekend and the residents confronted with the virtually impossible task of obtaining 15,000 signatures within a period of only several days. They made no effort to do this. Instead, they turned to the lower court, seeking a declaration that the enactment of the bills was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the lower court's decision because petitions designed to take a bill to referendum may be circulated for signature at any time after a bill has been enacted by the General Assembly, without awaiting the Governor's signature. Therefore, the bill was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying the resident's their requested injunctive relief was affirmed.

 

535 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Rockville Fuel & Feed Co. v. Gaithersburg


No. 364, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


266 Md. 117; 291 A.2d 672; 1972 Md. LEXIS 722; 50 A.L.R.3d 583



June 14, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Levine, J.



DISPOSITION: Order of December 22, 1971, affirmed, the appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which denied the company's requested injunction that sought a declaration of the company's rights to construct and use a proposed concrete mixing plant.


OVERVIEW: The company contended that it had acquired a vested right to operate a concrete mixing plant that could not be defeated by the adoption of the amendment to the zoning ordinance, that the ordinance amendment was unconstitutional as applied to the company in that it was not general legislation but was aimed solely at the company and was applied retrospectively to the company, and that appellee city was estopped from taking any action denying the company the right to operate the concrete mixing plant. The court held that the company did not have a vested right to operate the concrete mixing plant because the company never obtained a building permit and never began construction of the plant. The court also held that the text to the zoning ordinance amendment was not unconstitutional as applied to the company because the amendment was not arbitrary, unreasonable, capricious, or discriminatory. Finally, the court held that the city was not estopped from taking action to deny the company the right to construct and operate the plant simply because the company relied on the former ordinance when initially purchasing the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the company's request for declaration that the company had a right to construct and use a proposed concrete plant.

Smith v. Westinghouse Electric Corp.


Nos. 312, 371, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


266 Md. 52; 291 A.2d 452; 1972 Md. LEXIS 717



June 13, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Sodaro, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments in Nos. 312 and 371 affirmed; costs in both appeals to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, representatives of decedent, sought review of two decisions of the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland) that dismissed their suits against appellee alleged tortfeasors regarding the wrongful death of the decedent.


OVERVIEW: Appellants' decedent was injured in an industrial accident, and on June 15, 1968, died as a result of his injuries. At that time, Md. Ann. Code art. 67, § 4(a) (Act) mandated a two-year statute of limitation after the death of the deceased person. Subsequently, the Act was amended to permit commencement within three years and the statute was to be applied retroactively. The wrongful death action was filed against appellees more than two years, but less than three years, after decedent's death. In both cases, the suits were dismissed because of expiration of the statute of limitations. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissals. The court found that the provision that purported to give retroactive effect to the Act was unconstitutional in that it violated the equal protection of laws provisions of the Fourteenth Amendment and the Declaration of Rights of the State of Maryland, art. 23. The court concluded that a statute placing burdens upon an individual or limiting his rights could be invalidated because of an arbitrary or unreasonable classification or discrimination, such as in the case at bar.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both judgments that dismissed appellants' actions against appellees for the wrongful death of their decedent as time-barred.

Prince George's County v. Beard


No. 380, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


266 Md. 83; 291 A.2d 636; 1972 Md. LEXIS 720



June 13, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Powers, Ralph W., C. J.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for further proceedings without affirmance or reversal; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which granted appellee taxpayers' motion to dismiss condemnation proceedings initiated by the county. The taxpayers asserted that there was no authority supporting condemnation and that such condemnation was unlawful under Md. Const. art. III, § 40.


OVERVIEW: A county initiated condemnation proceedings in order to construct an airpark. The trial court granted a motion to dismiss these proceedings which was filed by some interested taxpayers. That decision was remanded by the court but was not affirmed or reversed as it was unclear whether the county had the authority to initiate condemnation in this matter. Under Prince George's County Charter, §§ 818, 824 county projects could not be created or abandoned unless authorized by the county budget in accordance with a council vote. Similarly, under Prince George's County Charter, § 814 items could not be added to the budget except where required by state law. It was unclear whether or not the planned airpark was so authorized. Also, under Md. Const. art. III, § 40 private property could only be taken for public use. The determination of whether property was taken for private or public use was a judicial one and it was unclear in which category the airpark fell into.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the trial court's decision which sustained the motion to dismiss this matter without either affirming or denying it.

Marco Associates, Inc. v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 183, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


265 Md. 669; 291 A.2d 489; 1972 Md. LEXIS 989



June 7, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Shearin, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, corporate taxpayer, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) that affirmed an order of the tax court that refused to overturn a deficiency assessment imposed by appellee Comptroller of the Treasury.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a Subchapter S corporation, as permitted by 26 U.S.C.S. § 1371 et seq., with the consequence that its earnings were attributed to the corporation's stockholders, who paid the federal income tax thereon. In 1967, the legislature enacted Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 280(a), that brought capital gains and losses of a corporate taxpayer within the ambit of the Maryland income tax for the first time. Prior to that time, the taxpayer sold certain real estate and elected to realize the gain on an installment sale basis pursuant to 26 U.S.C.S. § 453. The stockholders liquidated the corporation prior to receipt and reporting of the total purchase price. As an incident to the liquidation, the corporation recognized on its federal tax return, the remainder of the gain which had been deferred. On its Maryland return, the taxpayer deducted the entire amount of the capital gain on the theory that it was not subject to tax under Maryland law in effect in year in which sale occurred. The court affirmed, however, and held that when the installment payments or the gain became a part of the taxpayer's income, whether or not a federal tax was payable, they were taxable under Maryland law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court rulings that upheld the deficiency assessment imposed on the taxpayer by the comptroller.

Borders v. Board of Education


No. 130, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


265 Md. 488; 290 A.2d 510; 1972 Md. LEXIS 972



May 15, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motions for Rehearing Filed May 17, 1972, and June 9, 1972; Denied May 17, 1972, and June 9, 1972, Respectively.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Dorsey, C. J. and Powers, Ralph W. and Meloy, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded for the passage of a declaration and order conformable to the views expressed in this opinion. Appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents of white school aged children, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which entered judgment in favor of appellees, members of school board, and dismissed the parents' petition, which sought declaratory and injunctive relief stopping the transfer of their white children to the remaining all black schools in the county.


OVERVIEW: The parents of white school aged children commenced suit against the school board and sought declaratory and injunctive relief stopping the school board from busing their children to the remaining all black schools in the county. After an evidentiary hearing, the trial court refused to issue the injunction, and the parents sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the order as modified. The court held: (1) the parents failed to make out any case supporting their claim that the transfer of the students presented any personal danger in terms of traffic safety and personal inconvenience of any substantial nature; (2) busing was required to achieve racial balance; (3) where it was possible to identify a segregated school, a prima facie case in violation of the Equal Protection cause was shown; (4) it was constitutionally permissible to require busing where de jure desegregation existed, and it was permissible to recognize the achieving of racial balance for one of the reasons of redrawing school attendance lines; and (5) the school board properly bused the students thus transferred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as modified the order of the trial court that entered judgment in favor of the school board and dismissed the parents' petition, which sought declaratory and injunctive relief stopping the transfer of their white children to the remaining all black schools in the county.

Hooks v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 299, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


265 Md. 380; 289 A.2d 332; 1972 Md. LEXIS 961



April 13, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Cole, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant Hooks.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a judgment absolute entered by the Baltimore City Court (Maryland) in favor of defendant, the comptroller of the treasury (comptroller) that affirmed decisions of the tax court, the comptroller, and the comptroller's hearing officer denying the taxpayer's claim for a refund of sales taxes paid by him and other taxicab lessees.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer leased a taxicab on a daily basis from an association of taxicab owners. Under the rental agreement with the association, the taxpayer and his colleagues paid a fixed amount for the use of the taxicab for a 12-hour period and agreed to purchase from the association all of the gasoline consumed during the period, at a price in excess of the market price. The association derived its income exclusively from the amount it charged for gasoline. A sales tax was collected by the association from lessee-drivers in accordance with the provisions of the Retail Sales Tax Act (act), Md. Ann. Code art. 81, §§ 324-371(1957, 1969 Repl. Vol.), on the amount paid as rent as well as on the amount paid for gasoline. On appeal, the court held that the tax paid for the lease of the taxicab was not exempt from taxation under §326(n) of the act; that the tax paid for the gasoline purchased from the association was not exempt from taxation under § 326(d) of the act; and that the act did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. The fact that lessee-drivers were required to pay a sales tax, while owner-drivers were not, was not an arbitrary distinction among businesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that affirmed decisions of the tax court and the comptroller denying the taxpayer's claim for a refund of sales taxes paid.

Annapolis v. Shearwater Sailing Club, Inc.


No. 302, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


265 Md. 280; 288 A.2d 887; 1972 Md. LEXIS 948



April 6, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Mayfield, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Annapolis sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by appellee sailing club. The lower court's decision was based on its conclusion that the mayor's decision on an administrative appeal was void because the appeal had not been timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The sailing club filed an application with the port wardens for permission to construct piers and other facilities on its waterfront property. The application was opposed by certain citizens. The port wardens granted the application and certain other citizens, who had not opposed the application, filed an untimely appeal with the mayor. They argued that they did not receive notice of the decision in time to file a timely appeal. The mayor heard their appeal and ruled in their favor, denying the permits sought by the sailing club. On appeal in the lower court, the lower court granted summary judgment to the sailing club, holding that the mayor's decision was void because there had been no timely appeal. The City appealed, representing the mayor's position. The court affirmed the lower court, but not on the ground that the appeal was untimely. Instead, the court ruled that the citizens who brought the appeal before the mayor did not have the right to appeal because they had not opposed the application before the port wardens. The right to appeal was granted only to those citizens who had been involved in the matter pending before the port wardens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Ammendale Normal Institute, Inc. v. Schrom Constr., Inc.


No. 184, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


264 Md. 617; 288 A.2d 140; 1972 Md. LEXIS 1177



March 6, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed March 17, 1972; Denied April 3, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Meloy, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) that denied it injunctive relief against appellee contractor in the property owner's action seeking the forfeiture of a license agreement that permitted the contractor to mine for sand and gravel.


OVERVIEW: The property owner and the contractor entered into a license agreement that permitted the contractor to mine for sand and gravel on the property owner's property in exchange for a monthly royalty payment. In a prior action, the property owner obtained a judgment declaring that the contractor was in arrears on the royalty payments, and he was directed to pay promptly the amounts due. No injunctive relief was granted in the previous action, and the property owner then filed a petition praying for the contractor to have been held in contempt because the payments previously ordered had not been made. The trial court found the contractor in contempt of the earlier decree but held that he had purged himself of it by subsequently making the payments due. The trial court therefore declined to order any injunctive relief prayed for, and the court affirmed. The court noted that the property owner was in essence seeking a forfeiture of the license agreement, and it observed that equity disfavored forfeitures. The court held that where the license agreement was silent as to the remedies available upon its breach, the property owner was not permitted to declare a forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying injunctive relief to the property owner in his action seeking the forfeiture of a license agreement entered into with the contractor.
