Ansell v. Howard County Council


No. 357, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


264 Md. 629; 287 A.2d 774; 1972 Md. LEXIS 1178



March 6, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed March 14, 1972; Denied March 14, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County; Mayfield, J.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded without affirmance or reversal for the making of a declaration that expresses the views herein contained. The appellant shall pay the costs. Mandate to issue forthwith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which dismissed his petition seeking a declaration that a resolution adopted by appellees, a county council and the president of a board of education, was null and void.


OVERVIEW: The council and president adopted a resolution that authorized the present to enter into contracts for the construction of certain schools. The taxpayer claimed that the resolution was unconstitutional, discriminatory, and illegal. The trial court dismissed his petition on the ground that he had presented no justiciable controversy that would entitle him to a declaration. The court held that there was a justiciable controversy, and the taxpayer had to be told that he could not prevail by a declaration rather than a dismissal. The resolution was a measure adopted by the council of a temporary and administrative character. The council had the power to adopt it. The taxpayer did not allege or prove that the council and president violated their trust or did anything they ought not to have done. If the State did not pay or reimburse Howard County for the cost of the school construction, the County could proceed in the fashion it had formally indicated by resolution.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case remanded without affirmance or reversal for the making of a declaration that expressed the views contained in its opinion.

Maryland Nat'l Bank v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 221, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


264 Md. 536; 287 A.2d 291; 1972 Md. LEXIS 1169



February 17, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Cardin, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trustee challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which upheld the decision of the tax court, affirming the tax assessment against the trust that was assessed by defendant state comptroller.


OVERVIEW: The trustee argued that the accumulated and undistributed net income of the trust estate, which resulted from a gain on the sale of capital assets, was not taxable to the trustee. The trustee disclosed the gain of the trust estate on fiduciary tax return, but paid no tax, on the theory that the income was being held for the benefit of nonresidents of the forum state. The comptroller disagreed with the trustee's interpretation and assessed a tax. The court affirmed the judgment because it was clear that undistributed capital gains were subject to income tax under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 313(b), regardless of whether § 313(b) was read as an exclusion or an exemption. In other words, the court held that it was irrelevant whether the beneficiaries of the trust were residents or not.


OUTCOME: The judgment upholding the assessment of a tax against the gains of a trust was affirmed.

546 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Barranca v. Prince George's County


No. 283, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


264 Md. 562; 287 A.2d 286; 1972 Md. LEXIS 1171



January 20, 1972  
February 17, 1972, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowen, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commissioners challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which held that the commissioners were lawfully removed from their offices, and that appellee county executive was empowered to remove from office for cause without the concurrence of the county council any such commissioner appointed from the county.


OVERVIEW: The terms of the commissioners had expired but they continued as commissioners holding over until their successors were duly appointed. Prior to enactment of charter, the board of county commissioners governed the county. Under the charter, the county executive and county council governed. The commissioners argued that the removal of public officials was inherently an executive act and that the charter preserved the doctrine of separation of governmental powers. The court reversed. A proper and perceptive reading of the relevant constitutional and statutory provisions required a finding that the power of removal for cause of a county commissioner was in the hands of both the county executive and the county council. The court found no reason why "the traditional American practice" that the executive proposes and the legislature disposes should not be applicable under state law both to appointments to and removal from the office of commissioners from the county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders.

Thomas v. Solis


No. 66, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


263 Md. 536; 283 A.2d 777; 1971 Md. LEXIS 716



November 18, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Loveless, J.



DISPOSITION: Order sustaining demurrer of Solises reversed and sustaining demurrer as to State affirmed, case remanded for further proceedings in conformity with this opinion, appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which sustained appellee state officials' demurrers to the father's petition to have himself judicially declared the father of his three illegitimate children. The father also sought review of an order that sustained appellee mother and stepfather's demurrers to the same petition.


OVERVIEW: The father filed an action for a declaration that he was the father of the children. He also sought a declaration that certain statutes relating to his rights regarding the children were unconstitutional. The children's mother and stepfather demurred to the first part of the petition, while the state officials demurred to the second. The trial court sustained both demurrers. The father sought review. The court reversed as to the mother and stepfather and affirmed as to the state officials. The court found that the father stated a claim for the legitimatization of the children under Md. Ann. Code art. 93, § 1-208 (1969). Although that section dealt specifically with legitimization in the context of inheritance rights, the court held that there was no reason why it should not have applied generally to determine the rights of a putative father. Thus, the court held that under proper circumstances the father of illegitimate children was entitled to bring an action for a judicial declaration that the children were his pursuant to § 1-208. The court further found that the father had pleaded matter that supported his claim, including his open and notorious acknowledgement of the children.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that sustained the mother and stepfather's demurrer to the father's petition to have himself declared to be the father of his illegitimate children. The court affirmed an order that sustained the state officials' demurrer to allegations that certain statutes were void.

 

548 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Baltimore v. Silver


No. 43, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


263 Md. 439; 283 A.2d 788; 1971 Md. LEXIS 707



November 15, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Dehearing Filed December 3, 1971; Denied December 8, 1971. Notice of Appeal to Supreme Court of United States Filed January 6, 1972.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Harris, J.



DISPOSITION: The portion of the order denying summary judgment affirmed, case remanded for the limited purpose of having the court restate its order to include therein a declaration of rights in conformance with the views expressed in this opinion; appellants to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Baltimore (city) challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which denied its motion for summary judgment and dismissed its declaratory relief proceeding against appellee riot victims which alleged that application of Md. Code Ann. art. 82 resulted in due process and equal protection violations.


OVERVIEW: In a case involving damages suffered by the riot victims, the city brought an action for a declaration that application of Md. Code Ann. art. 82 (art. 82) resulted in due process and equal protection violations. On appeal, the city contended that the trial court erred in denying its motion for summary judgment and dismissing its declaratory relief proceeding. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of the city's motion for summary judgment and remanded the case for the lower court to restate its order including a declaration of the parties' rights. The provision at issue, art. 82, was not intended to be based on the requirement that a municipality had to have control over a police force to have the ability to suppress riots. Failure to have control over a municipal police force did not excuse a municipality from endeavoring to suppress or contain riots or tumultuous actions by using other reasonable means available. It was for the trier of facts to determine what action the city could or should have taken, if any, in the exercise of "reasonable diligence" to prevent or contain the situation at issue.


OUTCOME: In this action concerning the constitutionality of the application of art. 82, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of the city's motion for summary judgment, and remanded the case for the lower court to restate its order including a declaration of the parties' rights.

 

549 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Vermont Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Wicomico County


No. 17, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


263 Md. 178; 283 A.2d 384; 1971 Md. LEXIS 684



October 18, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County; Travers, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, appellant to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), which held that appellee county obtained a valid and prior lien on the realty that secured the creditor's loan and that the county's entire tax claim should have been paid out of the proceeds of the sale of the realty.


OVERVIEW: The creditor loaned money to a business. The loan was secured by the real estate owned by the business. The business defaulted, the creditor foreclosed on the property, and a sheriff's sale was held. The county filed a claim against the proceeds of the sale for the payment of delinquent personal property taxes. The trial court held that the county obtained a valid and prior lien on the realty and ordered the county's entire tax claim paid out of the proceeds of the sale. The creditor sought review and the court affirmed. The court found that under Wicomico County, Md., Code Pub. Loc. Laws § 248 (1959), all taxes due and owing upon both real and personal property constituted a prior lien against all of the taxpayer's real estate. Additionally, the court found that Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 202(b) (1969) provided that whenever a sale of either real or personal property was made, all sums due and in arrears for state taxes were to be paid first. The court held that the local law was not invalid because it did not conflict with the more general state provision. Thus, the court determined that the county was entitled to a lien against the real property for the personal property taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that held that the county's rights to the proceeds of a foreclosure sale had priority over those of the creditor.

 

550 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Katzenberg v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 25, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


263 Md. 189; 282 A.2d 465; 1971 Md. LEXIS 685



October 18, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Cardin, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment of the Baltimore County Court (Maryland) that affirmed the denial of the taxpayers' claim for a refund of Maryland capital gains taxes paid on installment sales pursuant to the newly enacted 1967 Maryland income tax law, Md. Ann. Code art. 81, §§ 279-283, 287-289, 323-323A.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayers challenged the lower court's affirmance of the denial of its request for a refund of capital gains taxes paid on installment sales. The taxpayers challenged the constitutionality of the newly enacted 1967 Maryland income tax law (Act), on the grounds of its retroactive application to payments they received under installment agreements and uniformity. The court affirmed the lower court judgment. The court found that the Act was not directed at payments received from installment sales before the date of its enactment, but that it was the taxpayers' election to defer recognition of their gain until the years 1967 and 1968, when the Act was fully operative, that brought their gains within its scope. The court rejected the taxpayers' uniformity argument that the unequal treatment of taxpayers who did and did not elect to report capital gains on an installment basis made the tax imposed by the Act arbitrary and discriminatory and thus unconstitutional. The court also held that because Maryland had an income tax at the time of the taxpayers' sales, they knew or should have known that the fact that capital gains were not taxed was no more than an exemption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment that affirmed the denial of the taxpayers' claim seeking a refund of Maryland capital gains taxes paid on installment sales.

Village Books, Inc. v. State's Attorney for Prince George's County


No. 37, September Term, 1971


Court of Appeals of Maryland


263 Md. 76; 282 A.2d 126; 1971 Md. LEXIS 674



October 13, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Powers, Ralph W., J.



DISPOSITION: Order modified and as modified affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an action against defendants, a corporation and related parties, seeking injunctive relief pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 418A (1971 Repl. Vol.) so as to prevent defendants from selling magazines alleged to be obscene. The Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) enjoined defendants from selling, distributing, or possessing with intent to sell or distribute 18 specified magazines. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' counsel informed a state's attorney that defendants intended to open an adult bookstore and furnished the state's attorney with samples of the books and magazines defendants intended to sell. At the hearing before the trial court, the state's attorney offered 21 of the samples as exhibits, declared them to be hard core pornography requiring no further proof, and rested his case. On review, the appellate court examined each of the 18 books and magazines that were the subject of the trial court's order. The court found that 13 of the samples, ten of which contained text and professional photographs of nude young adults with their genital areas conspicuously displayed, were not pornographic. As for the remaining 5 samples, the appellate court agreed with the trial court's conclusion that they constituted hard core pornography. Finally, the appellate court rejected defendants' challenge to the constitutionality of the statute under which the instant action was brought, holding that the statute did not provide for prior restraint of presumptively protected literary materials and that defendants were not entitled to a jury trial on the issue of obscenity.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's order by deleting therefrom 13 specified magazines. As so modified, the court affirmed the trial court's order that enjoined defendants from selling, distributing, or possessing with intent to sell or distribute the specified magazines.

Turf Valley Associates v. Zoning Board of Howard County

Court of Appeals of Maryland


262 Md. 632; 278 A.2d 574; 1971 Md. LEXIS 960



June 29, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed July 19, 1971; Denied September 13, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County; Childs, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land owner sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which found that appellee county zoning board's deletion of a zoning ordinance that provided for planned communities was legally and effectively accomplished.


OVERVIEW: The land owner possessed several hundred acres of land which it had attempted to have rezoned for combined intense residential and commercial uses. The trial court ruled in favor of the land owner finding that the zoning board had acted arbitrarily and illegally in denying a change in the classification of the land. On appeal, the judgment was reversed. Subsequently, the zoning board deleted the zoning ordinance, which provided for planned communities. The trial court ruled in favor of the board holding the deletion to have been legally and effectively accomplished. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that there was no fundamental barrier to conferring on the legislative branch of a chartered county the right to constitute itself a zoning body and that the county charter had permitted the council to act as it did. Accordingly, the land owner's first appeal was dismissed as being moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order holding the zoning board's deletion of an ordinance was legally accomplished.

Morris v. Governor of Maryland

June 25, 1971  
September 17, 1971, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Evans, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which determined that the amendments to the Maryland Constitution that were enacted after a general election was held were valid and effective.


OVERVIEW: At the general election the voters in the State of Maryland approved eight amendments to Maryland's Constitution. The resident filed a petition seeking a declaration that each proposed amendment had been unconstitutionally placed on the ballot, and that each had been unconstitutionally submitted to the electorate. The court also determined that the ballot titles that were challenged by the resident were beyond successful attack. Appellee Governor's proclamation that the constitutional amendments were valid was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Prince George's County v. Laurel


No. 385, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


262 Md. 171; 277 A.2d 262; 1971 Md. LEXIS 921



May 14, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Loveless, J.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county planning commission and a board of commissioners, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which entered judgment in favor of appellee town in the town's declaratory judgment action to determine its right to rezone the land in controversy.


OVERVIEW: Exclusive authority for parks, planning, and zoning within a metropolitan district was vested in the commission and the board of commissioners. The town annexed a portion of land from the district and approved certain zoning classifications for the areas. The commission and the board refused to give any recognition to the attempted rezoning. The trial court determined that the town had exclusive planning and zoning authority over the annexed property and that neither the commission or the board had such authority. The trial court further held that the board and commission retained jurisdiction over buildings and infrastructure within the annexed property. The trial court further determined that 1965 Md. Laws 373 was unconstitutional. The court determined that the trial court properly determined the respective authority of the town, commission, and board under the amendment to Md. Ann. Code art. 23A, §§ 9(c), 19(p). The court found that the trial court erred in holding that 1965 Md. Laws 373 was unconstitutional because the trial court failed to recognize that 1965 Md. Laws 373 was a valid general law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment that related to the authority of the town, commission, and board, but reversed the portion of the trial court's judgment that determined that 1965 Md. Laws 373 was unconstitutional.

Madison Nat'l Bank v. Newrath


No. 322, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


261 Md. 321; 275 A.2d 495; 1971 Md. LEXIS 1086



March 29, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed April 28, 1971; Denied May 3, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Pugh, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed and case remanded for the entry of a decree consistent with this opinion; appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which rendered judgment that the lien in favor of appellee trustees and lender was superior to appellant's lien on property owned by the borrower. The judgment appealed from was rendered in appellant's action to enjoin foreclosure of the deed of trust held by appellee lender on the borrower's property.


OVERVIEW: Appellee lender made a loan to borrower partner, receiving as security therefor a deed of trust on property that he had contributed to the partnership. Appellee also obtained from borrower a security interest in the partnership, but did not record the deed. Appellant creditor made two loans to the same borrower, receiving an assignment in trust to the partnership property perfected by the filing of a financing statement. Appellant thereafter filed an action to enjoin appellee from foreclosing the deed of trust. The trial court held that appellee's security interest had priority over that of appellant's. Appellant sought review. The court reversed, finding that the borrower's interest in partnership property could not be conveyed by the partner because the property was no longer his, it belonged to the partnership. The court rejected appellee's argument that it had a valid interest in the partnership, finding that it failed to perfect the interest by filing a financing statement as required by U.C.C. § 9-302. The court found that under the Uniform Commercial Code the first assignee to perfect a lien would prevail and found that appellant had perfected its lien first.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that the lien in favor of appellee trustees and lender had priority over that of appellant creditor, because the borrower could not give a valid security interest in property he contributed to a partnership because the property had become partnership property. The court held that appellant's lien, although later in time, had priority because it was a valid security interest properly perfected.

Bruce v. Director, Dep't of Chesapeake Bay Affairs


No. 351, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


261 Md. 585; 276 A.2d 200; 1971 Md. LEXIS 1110; 2 ERC (BNA) 1810; 1 ELR 20271



March 9, 1971  
April 16, 1971, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing and to Recall Mandate Filed March 17, 1971; Denied March 17, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Somerset County; Duer, C. J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fishermen challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland), which upheld the constitutionality of Md. Ann. Code art. 66C, §§ 322 and 700(a), 700(c) and 700(i) (Repl. Vol. 1970) and dismissed the fishermen's bill of complaint against appellee state government officials.


OVERVIEW: The fishermen were residents of Somerset County and sought a declaration that Md. Ann. Code, art. 66C, §§ 322 and 700, which restricted the taking and catching of crabs and oysters in Maryland, were illegal, unconstitutional, and void. The fishermen filed their bill of complaint, seeking injunctive relief against the state government officials charged with enforcement of the challenged statutes and of licensing persons to take and catch crabs and oysters in Maryland. The lower court upheld the constitutionality of the statutes and dismissed the fishermen's action. On appeal, the court reversed, concluding that the statutes were an unconstitutional exercise of police power. The court concluded that the fishermen had standing to sue because the statutory restrictions had a severe adverse economic effect on the fishermen. The court concluded that the statutes discriminated not only among the several watermen of the 13 tidewater counties in which crabs and oysters are found in marketable quantities, but also between residents of the counties and the remaining counties. The court further concluded that the statutory provisions had no reasonable relation to the public interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision which upheld the constitutionality of the residency requirements and territorial restrictions on licensing commercial fishermen.

Maryland Community Developers, Inc. v. State Roads Com.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) rendered upon a jury verdict, which awarded the landowner compensation for appellee State Roads Commission of Maryland's (commission) taking of the landowner's property.


OVERVIEW: The commission took the landowner's property by condemnation for the purpose of building a superhighway. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which awarded the landowner $ 8,600 per acre for his land in the eminent domain proceeding.

Rapley v. Montgomery County


No. 298, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


261 Md. 98; 274 A.2d 124; 1971 Md. LEXIS 1060



March 2, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Mathias, Joseph M., J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which entered a judgment in favor of appellees--county, county council, and finance director--in the taxpayers' suit to recover a transfer tax they paid on the sale of their agricultural land.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers acquired legal title to the subject farmland and sold part of it to an enterprise. When the deed was recorded, the taxpayers paid, under protest, a county transfer tax of six percent on the sale price. The taxpayers then initiated a suit against appellees to recover the tax wrongfully paid, claiming that the county code imposing the tax was unconstitutional and did not apply to the taxpayers. The trial court entered judgment for appellees, and the court affirmed on appeal, holding that the taxpayers could not recover their taxes paid under protest because no statute afforded the taxpayers a refund and because there was no right at common law to recover taxes voluntarily paid under a mistake of law, even if paid under protest and even if the statute under which the tax was paid was later determined to be unconstitutional or invalid. The taxpayers could not recover under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 213 (1957), because the tax was not paid to the state or a state agency; nor could they recover under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 214, because the tax was not an ordinary tax. Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 215 did not extend to recovery of the tax at issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the county, county council, and finance director in the taxpayers' suit to recover a transfer tax they paid on the sale of their agricultural land.

Bartholomey v. State


No. 106, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


260 Md. 504; 273 A.2d 164; 1971 Md. LEXIS 1255



February 2, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Charles County; Digges, C. J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences entered in the Circuit Court of Charles County (Maryland). Defendant was convicted of two counts of murder, assault with intent to murder, and escape. Defendant received the death penalty for the murder convictions and 10 years on the other charges, which ran concurrent to each other, but consecutive to the murder charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was being detained at the county jail on warrants when he escaped from the jail, and during the escape he shot and killed the sheriff and a deputy sheriff. He also shot at another person who was at the jail speaking with the sheriff. Defendant was convicted of two count of murder, assault with intent to murder, and escape. He received the death penalty for the murder convictions. On appeal, the court affirmed the decisions of the trial court. The court held that the imposition of the death penalty was not cruel and unusual punishment under either the Maryland or U.S. Constitutions. There was evidence that identified defendant as the perpetrator of the crimes charged. Defendant testified on his own behalf in an attempt to sustain his plea of not guilty by reason of insanity, not to produce mitigating evidence. It was acceptable for the trial judge to ask questions of an expert witnes, and to assist the prosecutor in expediting the witness's testimony. Defendant's counsel was not incompetent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, assault with intent to murder, and escape. The court also affirmed the imposition of the death penalty for the murder convictions.

Malmar Associates v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 173, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


260 Md. 292; 272 A.2d 6; 1971 Md. LEXIS 1235



January 6, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; DeBlasis, J.



DISPOSITION: Order of February 26, 1970, affirmed, the appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which sustained appellee commissioners' decision to deny the applicant's request for a special exception to a local zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The applicant owned land that was zoned multiple-family, medium-density. It planned to erect an apartment building, which was divided into three sections. The first section was completed before Prince George's County, Md., Zoning Ordinance No. 380 (1968) was passed. A special exception was required for the other sections, pursuant to the ordinance. The commissioner's denied the applicant's request for a special exception for the third section and the trial court sustained the denial. Based on the fact that school facilities were not available, the commissioners' decision was not arbitrary and capricious. The ordinance was not unconstitutional because the applicant did not have vested rights since no construction had begun on section three when the ordinance was passed. Further, the ordinance was not an unreasonable restriction on property and it did not constitute a denial of equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which sustained the commissioners' decision to deny the applicant's request for a special exception to a zoning ordinance.

OVERVIEW: A restaurant owner operated her business as a nonconforming use in a single-family residential neighborhood. 564 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Baltimore v. Charles Center Parking, Inc.


No. 113, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


259 Md. 595; 271 A.2d 144; 1970 Md. LEXIS 836



November 13, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Carter, Joseph L., J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed. Costs to be paid by the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mayor and a city counsel, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which ruled in favor of appellee parking company in a zoning action.


OVERVIEW: The parking company filed suit against the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore seeking a declaration that Baltimore, Md., Ordinance 1(e)(4) was invalid and to enjoin the City from enforcing the city code. The trial court noted that § 1(e)(4) prohibited painted signs in an area where billboards and posterboards were clearly allowed and he concluded that there was no reasonable basis for that distinction. Therefore, § 1(e)(4) was held invalid. The court agreed and held that the parking company properly overcame the presumption in favor of the validity of legislative enactments through testimony and the absence of any showing by the appellants that the ordinance was not arbitrary or unreasonable in its classification. The court found no sound rationale for distinguishing between painted signs and billboards in the designated area of Baltimore.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Clinton Volunteer Fire Dept., Inc. v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 6, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


259 Md. 456; 270 A.2d 778; 1970 Md. LEXIS 821



November 10, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed November 30, 1970; Denied December 9, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Powers, Ralph W., J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, the appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant firemen sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which found in favor of appellee county in the firemen's action for specific performance of their employment contracts after they were discharged for holding positions as volunteer firemen in addition to their career service positions.


OVERVIEW: The Director of Fire Prevention for a county promulgated an administrative order prohibiting career firemen from holding volunteer memberships in the same company where they were employed and prohibiting them from holding certain ranks in other volunteer fire companies. The firemen were discharged after they accepted promotions in the volunteer fire companies in conflict with the Director's administrative order. The firemen filed an action to enforce their contracts, contending that they were not county employees and that 1966 Md. Acts ch. 745, amending Prince George's County Code Pub. Loc. Laws art. 17, § 32-18, was unconstitutional in violation of Md. Const. art. III, § 29. The trial court dismissed their bill of complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the contracts of employment that permitted the firemen not to be considered as county employees were null and void, in violation of 1966 Md. Acts ch. 745 and that ch. 745 did not violate the single subject or title requirements of Md. Const. art. III, § 29. The single subject of the act was fire companies in a certain county and the title was not deceptive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

566 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hebron Sav. Bank v. Salisbury


No. 7, September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


259 Md. 294; 269 A.2d 597; 1970 Md. LEXIS 808



October 19, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wicomico County; Travers, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, with costs, and case remanded for the further proceedings indicated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Wicomico County (Maryland), which was entered in favor of appellee city that held that the bank was not entitled to recover from the city for damages that it had allegedly suffered as a result of the city's demolition of a residence on which the bank held a mortgage.


OVERVIEW: The city determined that the residence on which the bank held a mortgage violated the housing code. After giving proper notice to the owners, the bank ordered that the house was to be burned. The city overlooked the bank's mortgage when it checked the land and tax records. After the house was destroyed, the bank brought an action against the city alleging that the city was required to give notice to the bank prior to demolition. On appeal, the court held that the city code required that notice be given to the bank because the bank, as mortgagee, had a vested or contingent interest in the property to be destroyed. The court ruled that the bank had to be given an opportunity to show the trial court that the property demolished had value and was not a nuisance when it was demolished. The court also ruled that under the circumstances, the city was not entitled to sovereign immunity. The court concluded that if the bank showed that the house had actual value when it was burned, then the demolition amounted to a taking of the bank's property for which the city had to pay compensation. The court reversed the trial court's order, which was in favor of the city.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, with costs, and remanded the case for the further proceedings to give the bank an opportunity to show the value of the property, if any, when it was destroyed. The court ruled that if the bank could show such value, then the bank would be entitled to compensation from the city.

 

567 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hillyard v. Board of Supervisors


No. 247 (Adv.), September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


259 Md. 150; 269 A.2d 42; 1970 Md. LEXIS 787



August 17, 1970  
September 17, 1970, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Mathias, Joseph M., J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) ruled that appellant candidate could not run for the House of Delegates from Delegate District One of Montgomery County because he had not lived for a year in that District. The candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On the candidate's appeal, the court stated that Md. Const. art. III, § 9 provided that no person could be eligible as a Senator or Delegate, who at the time of his election, was not a citizen of the State of Maryland, and who had not resided therein for at least three years. In the case at bar, the candidate had resided in Maryland for the specified three-year period and had been a resident of Montgomery County for the last year of that period. It was undisputed that he moved from another part of Montgomery County to Legislative District Number One of Montgomery County and had since been a resident of that District. An eligible candidate only had to be a resident of the district he sought to represent and had to have been a resident of the county for a year. The court held that the candidate was eligible to be a Republican candidate for the House of Delegates, Delegate District One of Montgomery County, Maryland.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and declared the candidate to be a Republican candidate for the House of Delegates, Delegate District One of Montgomery County, Maryland.

 

568 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Polen v. Cox


No. 362, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


259 Md. 25; 267 A.2d 201; 1970 Md. LEXIS 778



July 10, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dorchester County; Mace, J.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and cause remanded for the passage of a decree in conformity with this opinion, appellee to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant national church overseer sought review of an order Circuit Court for Dorchester County (Maryland), which declined to exercise jurisdiction over a property dispute between the national church and appellee local church minister.


OVERVIEW: The minister was previously a state overseer for the colored division of the national church. The national church merged its segregated branches into a single state division, and the minister's position as an overseer was no longer necessary. The trustees of the local church approved the lease of property owned by the national church to the minister, and his congregation subsequently withdrew from the national church, forming a new religious corporation. The national church overseer for the state filed a bill of complaint for injunctive relief to prevent the minister's use and control of the property. The trial court declined to exercise jurisdiction and dismissed the action. On appeal, the court reversed, concluding that the property dispute involved a neutral principle of law, which could be resolved without infringing upon the First Amendment rights of free exercise of religion. The underlying source of the controversy was not the national church's decision to abolish the bifurcated overseer structure. The hierarchical nature of the denomination and its provisions required the national church to retain property after a local church discontinued fellowship with the organization.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded for entry of a decree in favor of the national church overseer.

 

569 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Silberman v. Jacobs


No. 125 (Adv.), September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


259 Md. 1; 267 A.2d 209; 1970 Md. LEXIS 777



July 9, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Perrott, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed, the appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant land purchaser sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which entered judgment for plaintiff land sellers, and found that the provisions of the 1969 Md. Acts, ch. 3, § 3-202, which had abolished dower and curtesy, were constitutional, valid, and effective in regard to all fee simple properties owned by married persons on and after the effective date.


OVERVIEW: The land sellers had agreed to sell land to the purchaser, but the purchaser refused to accept the sellers' deeds without the joinder of the sellers' spouses on the deeds. The purchaser was concerned that § 3-202 was unconstitutional, and therefore, the spouses' joinder would be required to obtain title to the land free from any claims of dower or curtesy. On appeal, the court affirmed the decree, and found that § 3-202 was constitutional. The court reviewed the historical background of dower and curtesy, and found that in Maryland, dower was a common-law right of a surviving spouse, which, prior to the other spouse's death, was inchoate. Therefore, the spouse had no interest or estate in the other spouse's land prior to the death of that spouse which was capable of being mortgaged, pledged or sold. The court held that no provision in either the state or U.S. Constitution prohibited the legislature from abolishing dower and curtesy because there was no taking of property without due process of law and no impairment of a contract, because the rights were not vested until death of the other spouse, and that the legislature had valid public policy reasons for the abolishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree, and found that the Maryland statute abolishing dower and curtesy was constitutional.

 

570 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Gordon v. Baltimore


No. 37 (Adv.), September Term, 1970


Court of Appeals of Maryland


258 Md. 682; 267 A.2d 98; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1044



July 9, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed July 31 1970; Denied August 17, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Carter, Joseph L., J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland) dismissing his complaint that sought to enjoin defendant institute from transferring books to defendant library, the library from receiving books from the institute, and defendant city from participating in the transfer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that the terms of the relevant individual's original gift prevented a transfer to the library of title to, supervisory control over, and responsibility for, the books which comprised the institute's library. The court disagreed. The institute had the power to transfer the books at issue. The court held that where property was given to a charitable corporation for such uses as were within the scope of its corporate purposes, and where there was no clear intention on the part of the donor to create a trust, the gift was not void on the ground that it was for indefinite purposes or in conflict with the rule against perpetuities. It was clear that the transfer of the books to the library, subject to the individual's original instructions to his trustees, involved no breach of trust.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the taxpayer's action for injunctive relief.

Baltimore Import Car Service & Storage, Inc. v. Maryland Port Authority


No. 391, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


258 Md. 335; 265 A.2d 866; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1006



June 3, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Carter, Joseph L., J.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, case remanded for further proceedings conformable with this opinion, costs to abide the result.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign car importer sought review of an order by the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which entered a judgment in favor of appellees, a port authority and various associated entities, in an action brought by appellant to challenge appellees' contracts with one another. Appellant alleged violations of Maryland's conflict of interest statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 19A, but the circuit court found the contracts to be valid.


OVERVIEW: The importer filed suit for declaratory relief under Md. Ann. Code art. 31A. The bill prayed that the contractual arrangements between appellees regarding leases of a port terminal be declared void and against public policy and that the port authority be required to enter into negotiations to lease a portion of the terminal to the importer. The importer also requested that the port authority be required to employ persons having no interest in the terminal facilities and that the other entities be required to remit to the port authority such monies as had been collected under the contractual arrangement and to account to the importer for such monies as had been collected from it. The court reversed. The court ruled that the facts alleged in the importer's petition, if supported by competent evidence, and not justified by the port authority, might well have established a course of conduct so repugnant to fair dealing as to entitle the importer to relief. The port authority's unexplained refusal to lease to the importer might well have involved the denial of equal protection guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment, which was binding on state agencies, such as the port authority.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

MacLeod v. Takoma Park


No. 359, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


257 Md. 477; 263 A.2d 581; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1328



April 2, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Levine, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner brought an action against defendants, the city, a wrecking contractor, and two members of the city's police force, alleging trespass, false imprisonment, and wrongful condemnation. The city demurred to all counts of the declaration. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) sustained the city's demurrer without leave to amend, and the property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the property owner argued that she had 180 days under Md. Ann. Code art. 57, § 18 to give notice of the alleged wrong. The trial court concluded that the city was statutorily immune from suit because notice of the alleged injury had not been given within 90 days. The court agreed with the trial court's interpretation of the statute. In actions against the counties of Anne Arundel, Calvert, Caroline, Cecil, Frederick, and St. Mary's and against any municipal corporation, regardless of whether the corporation was or was not located within any of the counties enumerated in § 18(a)(2), notice of the claim had to be given within 90 days. Further, the court rejected the property owner's contention that the constitutionality of the statute was imperiled by vagueness and uncertainty. Finally, the court held that because the property owner elected to proceed against the city in tort, claiming $ 25,000 in compensatory damages and $ 25,000 in punitive and exemplary damages in her declaration, the fifth count sought unliquidated damages and fell clearly within the notice requirements of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Williams v. Associated Professors of Loyola College

OUTCOME: The court modified and affirmed the order entering judgment in favor of the churches in appellants' condemnation proceeding.

Brukiewa v. Police Comm'r of Baltimore City


No. 149, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


257 Md. 36; 263 A.2d 210; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1283



February 13, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Sodaro, J.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, with costs, and case remanded for passage of an order reversing the disciplinary actions of the police commissioner against appellant, Brukiewa.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged the decision of the Baltimore City Court (Maryland), which upheld a police disciplinary board finding that the police officer had committed conduct unbecoming a member of the police department and prejudicial to or tending to undermine good order, efficiency, or discipline of the department.


OVERVIEW: The police officer appeared on television and stated that the morale of the police department was at its lowest ebb. The police officer also stated that, in response to the question of what would happen to the police department within the next six months if the situation continued, "I feel the bottom is going to fall out of this city." The department disciplinary board placed the police officer on probation for six months, which was extended to 12 months by the police commissioner. The lower court upheld the action. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the police officer did not go beyond the bounds of permissible free speech. The court held that nothing the police officer said was shown to be false, that his daily police duties had not been impaired by what he said, that his statements were not directed towards a superior with whom he would come in contact on a frequent basis, and that his statements had not been shown or found to have affected discipline or harmony or the general efficiency or effectiveness of the police department.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions to issue an order reversing the disciplinary actions taken against the police officer.

Glenarden v. Bromery


Nos. 320, 321, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


257 Md. 19; 262 A.2d 60; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1281



February 11, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three appeals from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowen, J.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the town, its former mayor, and the six councilmen who were elected in the regular election filed three appeals from ordered entered by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland). The circuit court had issued a mandatory injunction requiring the holding of a special election for all town offices.


OVERVIEW: By adopting a number of amendments to the town charter, the electorate replaced a mayor and a set of councilmen during their terms with another mayor and another set of councilmen. The displaced persons challenged the charter amendments to validly accomplish the change in terms and officials in a suit brought against appellees, the newly elected members and other citizens and taxpayers of the town. Appellants claimed that the special election was an exercise in the governmental process of recall for which there was neither constitutional nor statutory authority, and that the charter amendments reducing the terms of office from four to two years, if construed to be applicable and effective prior to the regular town election were both unconstitutional and illegal until that time. The court ruled that by Md. Const. art. XI-E, Md. Ann. Code art. 23A, the citizens were given the legal right to do exactly what a majority of them did, that was, amend the town charter to bring about the new form of government. The fact that the exercise of the right resulted in shortening the terms just as the exercise of a power to recall, had one existed, would have done was coincidental.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

577 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Great Atlantic & Pacific Tea Co. v. Paul


No. 205, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


256 Md. 643; 261 A.2d 731; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1202



February 6, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowie, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant food store sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which awarded compensatory and punitive damages to appellee shopper in his action for assault and battery, slander, and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A shopper claimed that a food store's employee falsely accused him of shoplifting, frisked him, and unlawfully detained him. The shopper recovered compensatory and punitive damages in his action against the food store for assault and battery, slander, and false imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the food store's employee testified that he stopped the shopper before he left the store, so there was no attempt by the shopper to leave without paying. Therefore, the court found that there was no showing of probable cause because there was no evidence that the shopper manifested control over the property in such a way that his intention to steal was unequivocal. The court found that there was sufficient evidence for the jury to find that the manner and method of the detention was not within the privilege "necessary for a reasonable investigation of the facts" because there was not a reasonable belief that the shopper had tortiously taken a chattel upon the food store's premises.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below in favor of the shopper in his action against the food store for assault and battery, slander, and false imprisonment. The court found that the food store did not have probable cause to detain the shopper because there was no evidence that the shopper manifested control over the property with the intention to steal.

Beauchamp v. Somerset County Sanitary Com.


No. 162, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


256 Md. 541; 261 A.2d 461; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1185



February 3, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Somerset County; Travers and Mace, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, the appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant American Legion post appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland), which found for plaintiff sanitary commission in its declaratory proceeding against the American Legion, in which it claimed that 1966 Md. Laws ch. 674 was unconstitutional and invalid.


OVERVIEW: The American legion had land within the sanitary commission's district, but claimed exemptions from water main and sewer charges under 1966 Md. Laws ch. 674 (the Act). The sanitary commission assessed water main and sewer charges for that land, and filed a declaratory proceeding in the trial court under Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Md. Code Ann. art. 31A, (1957), alleging that the Act was unconstitutional and invalid. The trial court declared the Act unconstitutional and void and found that the lands of the American Legion was subject to the liens of the assessments levied by the sanitary commission for 1966, 1967 and 1968. The American Legion appealed and the court affirmed. The court held that the Act was a "special act" in a statutory plan that was already covered by a public general law. The court found that the practical effect and the effect intended by the sponsors of the Act was to exempt the American Legion from any assessment or charge by the sanitary commission, and, in effect, applied to one taxpayer only and to the lands of that one taxpayer. The court noted that such a "special" act was unconstitutional under the provisions of Maryland Const., art. III, § 33.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Wicomico County v. Todd


No. 260, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


256 Md. 459; 260 A.2d 328; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1175



January 9, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County; Travers, J.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed in part and reversed in part, and case remanded for passage of a decree expressing the views herein, costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), which declared that a bill authorizing the issuance of general obligation bonds was properly vetoed by the county council, but that the council had no authority to enact a substitute bill that was substantially the same as the vetoed bill.


OVERVIEW: A taxpayers group presented a petition for the first bill to be submitted to a referendum. The county council vetoed the bill, but later enacted a substitute bill that was substantially the same. Opponents sought a declaration that the veto was invalid and the substitute bill never took effect. The trial court upheld the veto, but not the enactment of the substitute bill. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The council had the power to veto the first bill and to enact the substitute bill. The council acted in good faith for proper and appropriate governmental reasons in enacting the substitute bill and not merely to avoid the referendum on the first bill. The feeling of an emergency induced by a growing school population and inadequate educational facilities, and rising costs of money and construction prompted the council to avoid a delay of several years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's declaration that the first bill was properly vetoed, but the court reversed the trial court's declaration that the substitute bill was improperly enacted, and the court remanded for further proceedings.

 

580 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Villa Nova Night Club, Inc. v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 187, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


256 Md. 381; 260 A.2d 307; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1168



January 7, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Carter, Joseph L., J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cabaret sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which dismissed its action against appellee Comptroller of the Treasury of the State of Maryland seeking to have declared Md. Ann Code art. 81, §§ 402, 403 (Supp. 1969) to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The cabaret argued that § 402, which imposed a tax on admissions and amusements, and § 403, distinguished between the taxpayers upon whom the taxes were imposed. The laws distinguished between businesses that charged a direct admission charge for entry, and those that charged an indirect admission by increasing the price of food and drinks, etc. This difference in treatment created a sub-classification of taxpayers who were required to pay their tax calculated on an entirely different basis than others. The cabaret argued that this was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the statutes were constitutional and the court affirmed. The court held that the classifications did not deny equal protection, but were simple and appropriate classifications of taxpayers. The legislature, in passing a revenue measure, had the power to classify, and could have imposed varying tax burdens on different groups. It was only when the attempted classification had no reasonable basis in the nature of the businesses classified and burdens were imposed unequally on taxpayers between whom there was no real difference that the courts would interfere.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

581 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hillyard Constr. Co. v. Lynch


No. 168, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


256 Md. 375; 260 A.2d 316; 1970 Md. LEXIS 1167



January 7, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Worcester County; Prettyman, J.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed, costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a construction company and a partner, challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland), which denied appellants' motion to quash the writs of summons and dismiss the declaration filed by appellees, homeowners and their corporation, in an action for damages alleged to have resulted from the breach of two contracts for the construction of town houses.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that venue did not lie against them in Worcester County under Md. Ann. Code art. 50, § 5 (1957, Repl. Vol. 1968), which by its title governed venue in suits against joint obligors, because they were not jointly liable on the contracts in question. On appeal, the court disagreed but dismissed the appeal on other grounds. Section 5 was repealed and reenacted by 1953 Md. Laws ch. 206, which was dispositive of appellants' argument because the article and section headings of its predecessor were works of the codifier. In any event, the court concluded that ch. 206 was intended to permit a contract action on which two or more defendants were allegedly obligated to be brought in the county where any one of the defendants resided or regularly did business. Because appellees' declaration alleged that appellants and their fellow defendants were joint obligors, the court held that the motion to quash was properly denied. However, the court dismissed the appeal of its own accord under former Md. R. 835(a)(2) because the denial of appellants' motion to quash was an interlocutory order, rather than a final judgment from which an appeal could be taken.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

582 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Milestone v. Washington Suburban Sanitary Com.


No. 104, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


256 Md. 245; 260 A.2d 43; 1969 Md. LEXIS 646



December 29, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Filed January 28, 1970; Denied February 2, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Meloy, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which held that appellee Washington Suburban Sanitary Commission had not attempted to assess the landowner's parcel of land twice for benefit charges associated with the same sewer.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned a tract of land that fronted on a sewer line and that the commission identified as containing four blocks of land, he redeemed sewer benefit charges levied on two of the blocks, an apartment building subsequently was built on one of the blocks, and the commission assessed a multiunit sewer benefit charge for the apartment tract. The court affirmed the assessment, found that the property was broken up into parcels for assessment purposes and that the landowner's earlier redemption applied only to the two blocks. When the owner redeemed the sewer benefit on the two tracts, Prince George's County, Md., Code of Public Local Laws, § 1571(a) (1953) provided for assessment only on agricultural, small acreage, industrial, or business and sub-division property, but, by the time of the disputed assessment, a class was added for multiunit residential properties. The court held that, under Prince George's County, Md., Code of Public Local Laws, § 83-71(g), the commission was obliged to permit connection and to proceed to assess under the then applicable law, which by then provided a multiunit classification, and that the commission levied the assessment properly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the commission had not attempted to assess the landowner's property twice for the same sewer and that the commission's assessment was valid.

 

583 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


W. R. Grace & Co. v. Comptroller of Treasury, etc.


No. 22, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


255 Md. 550; 258 A.2d 740; 1969 Md. LEXIS 733



November 11, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Baltimore City Court; Sodaro, J.



DISPOSITION: Order of January 22, 1969, affirming the assessment of the appellee Comptroller of the Treasury, Retail Sales & Use Tax Division dated July 12, 1966, reversed, the assessment of the Comptroller of the Treasury abated, and the appellee to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of a decision of the Baltimore City Court (Maryland), which held that appellee comptroller of the treasury's assessment for use taxes upon two airplanes owned by the company and used by it regularly and exclusively for the transportation of passengers and property across state lines and national boundaries to various company plants throughout the Northern American continent were valid.


OVERVIEW: The comptroller assessed a use tax on two airplanes that the company owned and used to transport passengers and property across state lines and national boundaries to various company plants throughout the North American continent. The trial court affirmed the validity of the assessment of use taxes by the comptroller, holding that the airplanes owned by the company were employed regularly and exclusively in interstate and foreign commerce in the transportation of passengers. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that during the period of the assessment, the two airplanes were used exclusively as instruments of interstate commerce and the privilege of such use was not subject to local taxation because the language of the comptroller's Rule 64(c) exempted the airplanes from taxation. The court found that the two airplanes did not engage in any local activity that could have been realistically separated from their use in interstate commerce. The court held that the comptroller's attempted application of the use tax could not be sustained by reason of its repugnancy to the commerce clause of the United States Constitution and the provisions of the Maryland statutes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which held that the comptroller's assessment for use taxes upon two airplanes owned by the company and used by it regularly and exclusively for the transportation of passengers and property across state lines and national boundaries to various company plants throughout the Northern American continent were valid.

 

584 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hewitt v. Maryland State Board of Censors


No. 74, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


255 Md. 528; 258 A.2d 217; 1969 Md. LEXIS 731



November 10, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Sodaro, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant exhibitor sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) that held that two films were obscene under Md. Ann. Code art. 66A, § 19 (1965) in response to an application filed by appellee, the Maryland State Board of Censors.


OVERVIEW: The exhibitor claimed it had a right to show two films without the approval of the Board because a court hearing was not held within the time frame dictated by § 19. Under § 19, the Board was required to approve or disapprove a film within five days after submission. If the Board disapproved, it was required to apply to the circuit court within three days for a judicial determination whether the film was obscene. Then, the circuit court had to conduct a hearing within five days and enter an order approving or disapproving the film within the next two days. In the instant case, the circuit court held a hearing and issued an order on the seventh day following submission by the Board. The court on appeal affirmed. The circuit court decided the case within seven days following submission by the Board as required by the statute. The exhibitor received a final decision within the 15 days contemplated by the statute for the entire process and within seven days after the Board applied to the circuit court. The statutory scheme for film censorship was not violated because the hearing was not held within five days where the decision was issued within the seven days required by § 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order.

 

585 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Potts v. Governor of Maryland


No. 47, September Term, 1969


Court of Appeals of Maryland


255 Md. 445; 258 A.2d 180; 1969 Md. LEXIS 721



November 6, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Evans, J.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed, appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a Republican member of the Board of Election Supervisors of Prince George's County (Maryland), challenged a ruling of the Circuit Court for the County of Anne Arundel (Maryland), which denied the relief sought by the member in her action against appellees, the Governor and Secretary of State of Maryland. The member sought a declaratory decree that 1969 Md. Acts 1 (Act), governing the appointment of Board members, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Act required the appointment to the Board of two majority party members, whose gubernatorial candidate received the highest number of votes, and one minority party member, whose candidate received the second highest number of votes. When Maryland's Republican Governor was elected U.S. Vice President, a Democrat was elected as his replacement. As a result, the member argued that the Act unconstitutionally abolished her office and shortened her term and that it was an unlawful emergency bill because it was not prompted by a threat to the public health or safety. On appeal, the court disagreed. Under Md. Const. arts. II, § 13 and XVII, § 8, the member's two-year Board term naturally expired before the provisions of the Act affected the composition of the Board. Those provisions merely prescribed the qualifications of those who could be appointed to the Board upon expiration of the member's term and thereafter, and the legislative declaration of emergency was conclusive and not reviewable. Finally, because the terms of the member and those with whom she served expired before the Act impacted the Board, the court held that the case was moot, and the appeal was necessarily dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

586 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State's Attorney for Charles County v. Triplett


No. 364, September Term, 1968


Court of Appeals of Maryland


255 Md. 270; 257 A.2d 748; 1969 Md. LEXIS 708



October 14, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Charles County; Bowen, J.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded without affirmance or reversal for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion, the costs in the lower court and in this court to abide the result in the lower court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county officials, citing Md. Const. art. III, § 29, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Charles County (Maryland), which entered summary judgment in favor of plaintiff gasoline sellers finding unconstitutional Md. Ann. Code art. 56, § 144A (Repl. 1964), which banned the use of promotional games in the selling of gasoline.


OVERVIEW: The gasoline sellers argued on appeal that Md. Ann. Code art. 56, § 144A (Repl. 1964) denied them due process of law and equal protection of the laws. The court remanded without affirmance or reversal. The court noted that Md. Const. art. III, § 29, which provided that the subject of legislation be described in its title, required that a restriction in the title of an act had to either confine the operation of the act to conform to that restriction if that construction were possible or, if such a construction were not possible, render the act void to the extent of the conflict between the restriction in the title and the provisions in the body of the act. The court determined that the trial court should not have granted summary judgment declaring Md. Ann. Code art. 56, § 144A (Repl. 1964) unconstitutional for denying due process and equal protection because such a denial was not apparent on the face of § 144A, especially in view of the possible restrictive effect of the provisions of its title upon its construction.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the gasoline sellers' action against the county officials, challenging the constitutionality of a ban on the use of promotional games, to the trial court, without affirming or reversing the trial court's summary judgment in favor of the gasoline sellers, for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion.

Arundel Corp. v. Board of Zoning Appeals


No. 230, September Term, 1967, No. 305, September Term, 1968


Court of Appeals of Maryland


255 Md. 78; 257 A.2d 142; 1969 Md. LEXIS 682



October 7, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals, consolidated for argument, from the Circuit Court for Howard County; Mayfield, J. in No. 230 and Evans, J., in No. 305.



DISPOSITION: Appeal in No. 230 (1967) dismissed. Order in No. 305 (1968) affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellant in both cases.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review in consolidated appeals of two decisions of the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland) related to a nonconforming use of property under Howard County, Md., Zoning Regulations (1954). In Case No. 230, the property owner sought review of the trial court's order in the property owner's action for injunctive relief, and in Case No. 305, it challenged the Board's finding of an illegal nonconforming use.


OVERVIEW: In Case No. 230, the property owner sought to enjoin the Board from conducting a hearing on the issue of whether the property owner's operation of a quarry was a valid non-conforming use where the property was classified as residential. The trial court sustained the Board's demurrer, and the hearing took place. The Board's decision that the operation of the quarry was an illegal non-conforming use was the basis of the appeal in Case No. 305. On appeal, the court dismissed the appeal in Case No. 230, and affirmed the trial court's judgment in Case No. 305. The appeal in Case No. 230 was rendered moot once the hearing had been conducted and the trial court issued a decision. In Case No. 305, the Board correctly determined that the operation of the quarry was an illegal non-conforming use. For a valid non-conforming use, the property owner had to establish the existence of a legal non-conforming use at the time of the enactment of Howard County, Md., Zoning Regulations (1954). The property owner failed to show that the operation of the quarry was valid under Howard County, Md., Zoning Regulations (1948), or that the quarry predated the adoption of the 1948 regulations.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the property owner's appeal in Case No. 230 as moot and affirmed the trial court's determination in Case No. 305 that the use of the property owner's property as a quarry was an illegal non-conforming use.

In re Johnson


No. 303, September Term, 1968


Court of Appeals of Maryland


254 Md. 517; 255 A.2d 419; 1969 Md. LEXIS 892



July 2, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Mathias, Robert B., J.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which denied his motion for a jury trial in delinquency proceedings brought by appellee State.


OVERVIEW: After the police officer was assaulted by some youths in a parking lot, he filed a petition in juvenile court against the minor and three other boys. The petition alleged that the minor was a "delinquent", and "in need of care and treatment". At the conclusion of a hearing before a master, the master recommended that the minor be found a delinquent. The minor filed exceptions to the master's report and filed a motion for a jury trial which was denied prior to the hearing de novo in the circuit court and again at the hearing. The minor argued that Md. Ann. Code art. 26, §§ 51-71A, 91-101, which created a system of juvenile courts, was unconstitutional because it made no provision for a jury trial. The court affirmed, concluding that (1) in Maryland, juvenile courts were courts of equity having the power and full right to decide without a jury every question of law and fact which might arise; (2) by the waiver permitted by § 54, the legislature chose to make alternate provisions for a jury trial; and (3) the proceedings of a juvenile court were not criminal in nature and its dispositions were not punishment for crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the minor's motion for a jury trial in delinquency proceedings.
